RPT-Wall St Week Ahead-Despite Amazon, brick stores are not dead yet - 路透新闻

{{20171119T180001.680+0000}}RPT-Wall St Week Ahead-Despite Amazon, brick stores are not dead yet(Repeats Friday story with no changes)

By Rodrigo Campos

NEW YORK, Nov 17 (Reuters) - Just in time for the Black Friday kick-off to holiday season shopping, stock market investors have been handed tools to bet on the decline of brick-and-mortar retail.

As of Friday, these tools were not yet for sale on Amazon.

An exchange-traded fund launched Thursday allows investors to bet on the decline of traditional retail and a second one doubles down by betting at the same time on the rise to supremacy of online sales.

The Decline of Retail Stores ETF and the Long Online Short Stores ETF are self-explanatory. The main index they track inversely, the equal-weighted Solactive-ProShares Bricks and Mortar Retail Store Index <.SOEMTYPR>, is composed of 64 retailers including Barnes & Noble , Sears , Office Depot , Macy's and Walmart , which have chains of physical stores as well as online presence.

They are not the only or the first planning for a decimation of the retail sector at the hands of Amazon and other online retailers. Research firm Bespoke introduced its Death by Amazon Index, currently with 54 components, in 2012.

The trend to online shopping is not new, but with online taking only a fraction of all retail sales, the ETFs expect to capitalize on the long-term trend.

"Online penetration is about 10 percent right now so there is a long way ahead for the strategy in our opinion," said Michael Sapir, CEO of ProShare Advisors in Bethesda, Maryland.

"A minority of brick and mortar (retailers) will be able to make the transition and it is going to be expensive and painful."

So far this year, the S&P 500 retail index <.SPXRT> is up 20 percent but only half of its 29 components have had a positive price return. Amazon , up over 50 percent this year at $1,129.88, has alone added $192 billion in market capitalization in 2017. The full index has gained roughly $230 billion.

Glen Kacher, whose Light Street Capital Management hedge fund was up 53 percent from January to October, said he is "shorting almost every retailer," betting their share prices will fall.

Kacher said many big retailers have failed to adapt to changing customer preferences, lagging even some corner delis that now use technology that lets people buy their breakfast sandwiches and coffee in seconds with the tap of a finger.

"The retailing industry is going to be an apocalypse," he said, without identifying which retailers will go down in flames. "Anyone working in the consumer retailing industry ... should be training for a new job."

For a graphic on retailers' market value see (http://reut.rs/2zLFXiN)

CLICK AND MORTAR

Reports of the death of brick and mortar retail could be mildly exaggerated, however.

Retail and food service sales in the United States during the first three quarters of 2017 totaled $4.78 trillion, with the $484.4 billion in September a monthly record high, according to U.S. government data.

About 164 million Americans plan to shop in the coming Thanksgiving weekend, including on Black Friday and Cyber Monday, according to the National Retail Federation.

Results from this week show the battle for consumers is far from lost at physical stores. Walmart, for instance, said third-quarter U.S. sales growth online and in-store was the strongest since 2009. [nL1N1NM0OQ]

A combination of online presence and easy access for consumers known as 'click and mortar' will allow some names to survive by letting their customers browse all their options online while offering the convenience of a quick pickup of the product on their drive home.

Shares of Walmart touched a record high on Friday, as did those of Home Depot , which earlier in the week raised its full-year profit and sales forecasts. [nL3N1NK4H3]

They are one of two kinds of retailers that analysts said would be better able to weather the online retail storm. Size will matter, and with more than 5,000 U.S. stores at Walmart and over 2,200 Home Depots in North America, their distribution network will be a key lifeline.

"Walmart is transforming itself into a major competitor of Amazon," said Chad Morganlander, portfolio manager at Washington Crossing Advisors in Florham Park, New Jersey.

"Our belief is there will be some winners on brick and many online retailers will start looking more traditional."

The other retailers seen surviving are those in search of a small niche that will allow them to keep margins growing, countering the trend of ever-smaller margins online.

"Unless you know exactly what you're going to order and it is mass market, you don't go to Amazon," said Kim Forrest, senior equity research analyst at Fort Pitt Capital Group in Pittsburgh.

"Holiday shopping means meaningful gifts. If you're a good retailer you can take advantage of that."

<^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^ Amazon is almost half of S&P 500 retailers' market value http://reut.rs/2zLFXiN

^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^> (Reporting by Rodrigo Campos in New York; Additional reporting by Jennifer Ablan; Editing by Megan Davies and James Dalgleish) ((rodrigo.campos@reuters.com; @rodrigocampos; +1.646.223.6344; Reuters Messaging: rodrigo.campos.thomsonreuters.com@reuters.net)) ((Wall St Week Ahead runs every Friday. For the daily stock market report, please click [.N]))

U.S. RESEARCH ROUNDUP- Altria Group, Applied Materials, Square - 路透新闻

{{20171117T225656.790+0000}}U.S. RESEARCH ROUNDUP- Altria Group, Applied Materials, SquareNov 17 (Reuters) - Wall Street securities analysts revised their ratings and price targets
on several U.S.-listed companies, including Altria Group, Applied Materials and Square, on
Friday.

HIGHLIGHTS

* Altria Group Inc : Jefferies raises target price to $72 from $71

* Anadarko Petroleum Corp : BMO raises to outperform from market perform

* Applied Materials Inc : Morgan Stanley raises target price to $61 from $56

Wall St Week Ahead-Despite Amazon, brick stores are not dead yet - 路透新闻

{{20171117T220657.063+0000}}Wall St Week Ahead-Despite Amazon, brick stores are not dead yetBy Rodrigo Campos

NEW YORK, Nov 17 (Reuters) - Just in time for the Black Friday kick-off to holiday season shopping, stock market investors have been handed tools to bet on the decline of brick-and-mortar retail.

As of Friday, these tools were not yet for sale on Amazon.

An exchange-traded fund launched Thursday allows investors to bet on the decline of traditional retail and a second one doubles down by betting at the same time on the rise to supremacy of online sales.

The Decline of Retail Stores ETF and the Long Online Short Stores ETF are self-explanatory. The main index they track inversely, the equal-weighted Solactive-ProShares Bricks and Mortar Retail Store Index <.SOEMTYPR>, is composed of 64 retailers including Barnes & Noble , Sears , Office Depot , Macy's and Walmart , which have chains of physical stores as well as online presence.

They are not the only or the first planning for a decimation of the retail sector at the hands of Amazon and other online retailers. Research firm Bespoke introduced its Death by Amazon Index, currently with 54 components, in 2012.

The trend to online shopping is not new, but with online taking only a fraction of all retail sales, the ETFs expect to capitalize on the long-term trend.

"Online penetration is about 10 percent right now so there is a long way ahead for the strategy in our opinion," said Michael Sapir, CEO of ProShare Advisors in Bethesda, Maryland.

"A minority of brick and mortar (retailers) will be able to make the transition and it is going to be expensive and painful."

So far this year, the S&P 500 retail index <.SPXRT> is up 20 percent but only half of its 29 components have had a positive price return. Amazon , up over 50 percent this year at $1,129.88, has alone added $192 billion in market capitalization in 2017. The full index has gained roughly $230 billion.

Glen Kacher, whose Light Street Capital Management hedge fund was up 53 percent from January to October, said he is "shorting almost every retailer," betting their share prices will fall.

Kacher said many big retailers have failed to adapt to changing customer preferences, lagging even some corner delis that now use technology that lets people buy their breakfast sandwiches and coffee in seconds with the tap of a finger.

"The retailing industry is going to be an apocalypse," he said, without identifying which retailers will go down in flames. "Anyone working in the consumer retailing industry ... should be training for a new job."

For a graphic on retailers' market value see (http://reut.rs/2zLFXiN)

CLICK AND MORTAR

Reports of the death of brick and mortar retail could be mildly exaggerated, however.

Retail and food service sales in the United States during the first three quarters of 2017 totaled $4.78 trillion, with the $484.4 billion in September a monthly record high, according to U.S. government data.

About 164 million Americans plan to shop in the coming Thanksgiving weekend, including on Black Friday and Cyber Monday, according to the National Retail Federation.

Results from this week show the battle for consumers is far from lost at physical stores. Walmart, for instance, said third-quarter U.S. sales growth online and in-store was the strongest since 2009. [nL1N1NM0OQ]

A combination of online presence and easy access for consumers known as 'click and mortar' will allow some names to survive by letting their customers browse all their options online while offering the convenience of a quick pickup of the product on their drive home.

Shares of Walmart touched a record high on Friday, as did those of Home Depot , which earlier in the week raised its full-year profit and sales forecasts. [nL3N1NK4H3]

They are one of two kinds of retailers that analysts said would be better able to weather the online retail storm. Size will matter, and with more than 5,000 U.S. stores at Walmart and over 2,200 Home Depots in North America, their distribution network will be a key lifeline.

"Walmart is transforming itself into a major competitor of Amazon," said Chad Morganlander, portfolio manager at Washington Crossing Advisors in Florham Park, New Jersey.

"Our belief is there will be some winners on brick and many online retailers will start looking more traditional."

The other retailers seen surviving are those in search of a small niche that will allow them to keep margins growing, countering the trend of ever-smaller margins online.

"Unless you know exactly what you're going to order and it is mass market, you don't go to Amazon," said Kim Forrest, senior equity research analyst at Fort Pitt Capital Group in Pittsburgh.

"Holiday shopping means meaningful gifts. If you're a good retailer you can take advantage of that."

^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^> (Reporting by Rodrigo Campos in New York; Additional reporting by Jennifer Ablan; Editing by Megan Davies and James Dalgleish) ((rodrigo.campos@reuters.com; @rodrigocampos; +1.646.223.6344; Reuters Messaging: rodrigo.campos.thomsonreuters.com@reuters.net)) ((Wall St Week Ahead runs every Friday. For the daily stock market report, please click [.N]))

POINT MARCHÉS-Wall Street piétine en attendant des baisses d'impôts - Reuters (French)

{{20171117T213947.079+0000}}POINT MARCHÉS-Wall Street piétine en attendant des baisses d'impôts(Actualisé avec citation, volumes, dollar, marché obligataire, pétrole)

* Le Dow a perdu 0,43%, le S&P-500 0,26% et le Nasdaq 0,15%

* Une semaine volatile

* Agitation autour de 21st Century Fox

par Lewis Krauskopf

NEW YORK, 17 novembre (Reuters) - La Bourse de New York a fini vendredi par une séance de baisse une semaine volatile, marquée par les incertitudes entourant le projet de réforme fiscale aux Etats-Unis et des prises de bénéfices au terme d'une saison des résultats ayant globalement convaincu les investisseurs de la pertinence des valorisations actuellement élevées.

L'indice Dow Jones <.DJI> a perdu 100,12 points (-0,43%), à 23.358,24. Le Standard & Poor's 500 <.SPX>, plus large et principale référence des investisseurs, a cédé 6,79 points, soit 0,26%, à 2.578,85. Le Nasdaq Composite <.IXIC>, à forte composante technologique, a pour sa part fini en recul de 10,5 points (-0,15%) à 6.782,79.

Sur la semaine, le Dow a abandonné 0,27% et le S&P-500 0,13%, soit une deuxième semaine consécutive de baisse pour ces deux indices, tandis que le Nasdaq a gagné 0,47%.

"Nous avons assisté à une hausse correcte des actions récemment et ce ne sont que quelques jours de remous", pense Massud Ghaussy (Nasdaq Advisory Services).

Wall Street a volé de records en records depuis le début de l'année, encouragée notamment par les promesses de baisses d'impôts massives du nouveau président américain Donald Trump.

Les républicains, majoritaires dans les deux chambres du Congrès, se sont emparés du sujet mais représentants et sénateurs avancent encore pour l'instant deux projets différents de réforme fiscale. Si la Chambre des représentants a adopté jeudi son propre texte, le Sénat n'a pas encore voté le sien alors que les républicains y disposent d'une majorité plus courte et apparemment moins unie sur le sujet. [nL8N1NN0KT]

Les économistes interrogés par Reuters ne croient pas à une grande réforme fiscale d'ici la fin de l'année aux Etats-Unis et ils doutent même qu'elle stimule vraiment l'économie. [nL8N1NN55W]

"Je pense qu'il y a la crainte que (les républicains) ne soient pas en mesure de réunir suffisamment de soutien pour pouvoir déposer sur le bureau du président quelque chose de vraiment substantiel à promulguer", dit Jake Dollarhide, directeur général de Longbow Asset Management.

"La semaine a débuté avec beaucoup d'optimisme sur la réforme fiscale et je pense que nous avons un peu la gueule de bois à la fin de la semaine", ajoute-t-il.

FOOT LOCKER S'ENVOLE

Le Dow Jones a aussi souffert vendredi du repli de 2,16% de Wal-Mart sur des prises de bénéfices au lendemain du bond de plus de 10% du titre après les résultats trimestriels publiés par le géant américain de la distribution. [nL8N1NM4DO]

Foot Locker s'est envolé de 28,16%, de loin la plus forte hausse du S&P-500, alors qu'il avait auparavant chuté d'environ 55% depuis le début de l'année. Le distributeur de vêtements et de chaussures de sport a ravi les investisseurs avec ses résultats trimestriels meilleurs que prévu et la maîtrise de ses stocks, tout en n'excluant pas de faire légèrement mieux que ses prévisions sur l'ensemble de l'année.

Mêmes causes et presque mêmes effets pour le groupe de prêt-à-porter Gap , qui a gagné 6,99% après ses résultats trimestriels meilleurs que prévu et le relèvement de ses prévisions annuelles. [nL8N1NM7X5]

Le groupe de télévision et de cinéma Twenty-First Century Fox a profité des rumeurs circulant sur les convoitises que certains de ses actifs suscitent pour gagner 6,24%. Après Disney (-0,15%), le câblo-opérateur Comcast (-2,46%) et l'opérateur télécoms Verizon (+1,45%) pourraient être intéressés par certains actifs importants de Fox, ont rapporté des sources jeudi. [nL8N1NM7TV]

L'agitation autour du groupe de Rupert Murdoch a atteint Viacom (+10,38%), qui semble être aussi perçu comme une cible potentielle dans ce secteur.

Environ 6,3 milliards d'actions ont été échangées au cours de la séance sur les différents marchés américains, ce qui est inférieur à la moyenne de 6,8 milliards sur les 20 séances précédentes.

Sur le marché obligataire, la probabilité jugée élevée d'une nouvelle hausse de taux de la part de la Réserve fédérale en décembre continue de contribuer à l'aplatissement de la courbe des taux aux Etats-Unis.

Le rendement à deux ans des emprunts du Trésor a touché un pic de neuf ans pour une huitième journée consécutive à 1,73% tandis que son équivalent à 10 ans a reculé à 2,35%. En conséquence, l'écart entre ces deux rendements n'a jamais été aussi faible depuis novembre 2007.

Le dollar, pour sa part, semble pâtir des incertitudes sur la réforme fiscale et ses conséquences éventuelles sur la croissance américaine. Le billet vert a cédé 0,2% face à l'euro , remonté près de 1,18 dollar, et 0,28% face à un panier de devises de référence <.DXY>.

L'euro a pris plus de 1% face au dollar sur l'ensemble de la semaine, sa plus forte progression hebdomadaire depuis début septembre.

Les cours du pétrole ont progressé de plus de 2%, ce qui ne les a pas empêchés de subir un repli hebdomadaire après cinq semaines consécutives de hausse. [nL8N1NN5EC]

(Avec Sruthi Shankar à Bangalore; Bertrand Boucey pour le service français) ((paris.equities@reuters.com; Service économie, +33 1 49 49 53 87;))Copyright (c) 2017 Thomson Reuters

UPDATE 4-J.B. Hunt, Wal-Mart climb aboard Tesla's electric truck - Reuters News

{{20171117T213813.904+0000}}UPDATE 4-J.B. Hunt, Wal-Mart climb aboard Tesla's electric truck(Recasts throughout, adds context on regulatory pressure to cut diesel pollution)

By Arjun Panchadar and Eric M. Johnson

Nov 17 (Reuters) - Tesla Inc on Friday got high-profile orders from Wal-Mart Stores Inc and fleet operator J.B. Hunt for its future electric truck, but would-be customers indicated they are giving the big rig a try, not buying in volume.

Most of the customers who announced plans to put down $5,000 deposits for the Tesla Semi indicated they wanted to test a few of the vehicles. Wal-Mart said it plans to order a total of 15 Tesla trucks, five for the United States and ten for Canada. The company operates a fleet of about 6,000 trucks in the United States.

JB Hunt Transport Inc was the first major U.S. trucking company to announce an order for Tesla's new "Semi" electric trucks, saying it had reserved multiple vehicles for use on the U.S. West Coast. [nBw11VJ7Xa]

Hunt did not say how many of the vehicles it would reserve. Tesla unveiled the Semi on Thursday without specifying prices.[nL1N1NM1N4]

The early orders reflected the uncertainty about how the market for electric commercial vehicles will develop. About 260,000 Class-8 trucks are produced in North America annually, and that market has a value of about $28.6 billion, said Don Ake, vice president of commercial vehicles at FTR, an industry economics research firm.

The 500-mile (800 km) range between charges that Tesla Chief Executive Elon Musk promised on Thursday for the Tesla Semi is about half the range between fill-ups of a diesel Class 8 truck. Heavy batteries cut payload and add cost, potential deal killers for fleet buyers focused on operating cost per mile. [nL1N1NM1N4]

However, Tesla, and incumbent truck makers such as Daimler AG , Navistar International Corp and its partner Volkswagen AG are investing in electric trucks in a bet that the market will shift over the next decade.

For global truck makers, the biggest market for electric trucks will likely be China, where the government is moving aggressively to convert the transportation system to electrified vehicles.

Regulators around the world are ratcheting up pressure on the trucking industry to slash emissions of soot and carbon dioxide from diesel trucks. In the United States, the government has estimated that heavy-duty trucks represent 4 percent of vehicles on the road but account for 20 percent of carbon emissions. Under President Barack Obama, the United States required truck makers to boost fuel efficiency through 2027.

Separately, some cities and ports are discussing banning or heavily taxing diesel vehicles. The Ports of Los Angeles and Long Beach in Southern California have a goal of only having zero-emissions trucks by 2035. California is committing $140 million to subsidize low-carbon freight transportation.

Tesla has been trying to convince the trucking community that it can build an affordable electric big rig with the range and capacity to compete with relatively low-cost, time-tested diesel trucks.

It was not clear how many orders for Semis Tesla had in hand. Among companies announcing plans to acquire small numbers of Tesla trucks were Michigan retailer Meijer Inc [MEIJR.UL] and Canadian retail chain Loblaw , which has said it wants an entirely electric corporate vehicle fleet by 2030. [nL1N1NN1LM]

Some big logistics companies stayed on the sidelines. United Parcel Service Inc said the courier had nothing to announce regarding Tesla's vehicles but would always look for options that fit its needs.

Brad Pinchuk, chief executive of Dubuque, Iowa-based Hirschbach Motor Lines, said his firm was looking to test non-diesel big-rig options but needed longer ranges than Tesla could provide and speedier fuel-up times.

Pinchuk said he plans to buy two hydrogen-powered trucks made by Salt Lake City-based electric Nikola Motor Company when they are available in 2020.

"It's a different application – putting liquid hydrogen into tanks – so it will be very similar sort of situation to diesel," Pinchuk said. "You'd be able to fuel up. It would take about the same amount of time to fuel up a diesel and go about the same distance."

REUTERS SUMMIT-Big-name investors focusing on disruption in food, utilities in '18 - Reuters News

{{20171117T180513.999+0000}}REUTERS SUMMIT-Big-name investors focusing on disruption in food, utilities in '18(For other news from Reuters Global Investment 2018 Outlook Summit, see: http://www.reuters.com/summit/investment18)

By David Randall

NEW YORK, Nov 17 (Reuters) - Retail, utilities, restaurants and financial services should all brace for more disruption in the year ahead, according to big-name investors who took part in the Reuters Global Investment 2018 Outlook Summit in New York this week.

Glen Kacher, whose Light Street Capital hedge fund is one of the best-performing funds for the year to date, said he was shorting most of the retail sector out of concerns that bricks and mortar stores will continue to lose market share as customers shift purchasing to Amazon.com Inc , which is among his top holdings.

At the same time, large companies such as Wal-Mart Stores Inc are using point of sale technology that processes debit and credit card transactions at slower speeds than coffee shops that use readers from payments company Square Inc , he said.

"The idea that the deli has better technology than Wal-Mart is stunning," he said, adding that the coming year will prove to be an "apocalypse" for the sector.

The SPDR S&P Retail ETF , which tracks companies such as Tailored Brands Inc and Urban Outfitters Inc , is down 5.5 percent for the year to date.

Not all disruption looks to be a negative for entrenched companies, however.

Marc Lasry, the billionaire co-founder of Avenue Capital Group, said that his firm is raising $1 billion for a new hedge fund focusing on distressed debt in the utility industry, which is facing increased demand for energy just as new regulations make it increasingly difficult to build new power plants.

Avenue Capital has invested in Texas-based electric company Dynegy Inc and bought a power plant in California, Lasry said, citing low prices.

"There are huge opportunities there," Lasry said.

NOT SO BORING

Kera Van Valen, a portfolio manager at $48.6 billion Epoch Investment Partners, said improvements in meter technology is helping utility holdings such as PPL Corp cut its margins by allowing the company to be more efficient in its response to storms or outages.

"Even the utilities - which often people want to write off as boring and not exciting – can continue to grow through their use of technology," she said.

Along the same lines, McDonald's Corp is expanding its self-ordering kiosks and digital app to all of its 14,000 U.S. locations, allowing employees to concentrate more on other areas of the restaurant, as well as partnering with UberEats, the food-delivery service run by ride-hailing firm Uber Technologies Inc [UBER.UL].

"When you think about the Millennials and the tendencies that Millennials have, ordering from a kiosk is quite comfortable for them. It also makes McDonald's feel a little more relevant," Van Valen said, which should boost the company's growth and its ability to increase its dividends.

Other disruptions may boost productivity across a sector. Joachim Fels, global economic adviser and a managing director at Pimco, which has more than $1.69 trillion in assets under management, said that blockchain - a shared ledger of transactions maintained by a network of computers on the internet that powers the cyptocurrency bitcoin - could be a disruptive factor for financial services.

JP Morgan Chase & Co , American Express Co, and a consortium of energy companies including BP Plc and Royal Dutch Shell Plc have all announced plans for blockchain-based payments systems over the last month. Fels expects that the technology will continue to disrupt financial services even if enthusiasm dies down for bitcoin, which hit a record high just short of $8,000 on Nov 8.

"I think that could lead to a spurt in productivity in financial services," Fels said. "So that sounds to me like the next big thing."

Follow Reuters Summits on Twitter @Reuters_Summits

(Reporting by David Randall; Editing by Jennifer Ablan and Susan Thomas) ((David.Randall@thomsonreuters.com; 646-223-6607; Reuters Messaging: david.randall.thomsonreuters.com@reuters.net))

FACTBOX-Retail outlook for holiday shopping season - Reuters News

{{20171117T173557.600+0000}}FACTBOX-Retail outlook for holiday shopping seasonNov 17 (Reuters) - U.S. brick-and-mortar retailers are sharpening their online focus, keeping a tight leash on inventory and are cutting back on promotions as they head into the all-important holiday season.

Some retailers are also improving in-store experiences and sprucing up their mobile apps and websites to better compete with online behemoth Amazon.com Inc .

U.S. holiday sales are expected to increase 3.6 percent to 4 percent, getting a boost from an extra selling day and rising consumer confidence, according to the National Retail Federation. (http://reut.rs/2zMTyWy)

Here are retailers' outlook for the season:

DEPARTMENT STORES

Macy's Inc * Forecast a jump in online sales in the crucial holiday quarter and said it would maintain its tight grip on inventory. (http://reut.rs/2hyJlTu) * To improve both functionality and user experience on its shopping app as it expects a big jump in traffic. Its new loyalty program is also expected to give sales a lift in the quarter Kohl's Corp * CEO Kevin Mansell says the retailer is well-positioned for the holiday quarter with lean inventories, and expects strong sales from its online business, as well as active apparel and footwear. (http://reut.rs/2z9nIEw) * Raises lower end of its adjusted profit forecast for the year ending January 2018 to $3.60-$3.80 per share, compared with its previous forecast of $3.50-$3.80. Nordstrom Inc * Is looking to make shopping at its stores more convenient by rolling out new tweaks to its services. * Says it is in a good inventory position heading into the fourth quarter for both off-price and full-price products.

J.C. Penny Co Inc * Expects ongoing cost-cutting initiatives to help margins in the fourth quarter. (http://reut.rs/2AOP2Eq) * Says launch of Fenty Beauty by Rihanna will continue to drive sales and foot traffic to Sephora during the holiday season.

BIG-BOX RETAILERS Wal-Mart Stores Inc * Forecasts strong performance in the key holiday season. * Says it will double down on incentives and has tripled its online selections. (http://reut.rs/2j3aNJe) * To compete with Amazon, it will offer free two-day shipping on more than two million products when the order exceeds $35 and discounts for online orders picked up at stores. Target Corp * The company is gearing up for the holiday season by cutting prices and introducing delivery options to compete with Wal-Mart and online sellers, moves that can lure customers but crimp margins. (http://reut.rs/2hzUsvc) * Target expects flat comparable sales in the fourth quarter, with an upside potential for a 2 percent comp increase. CONSUMER ELECTRONICS RETAILER Best Buy Co Inc * Has added to its long-term policy of price-matching by offering free shipping for the Thanksgiving to Christmas period to take on Amazon. (http://reut.rs/2mCqLiA) * Expects Q4 adjusted earnings per share from continuing operations to be $1.89-$1.99, below analysts' average estimate of $2.01.

APPAREL RETAILERS Tapestry Inc * Says it is well positioned to drive positive comparable sales growth this holiday season due to its new collection and a differentiated luxury store experience. (http://reut.rs/2irWL4F) * However, results from its Stuart Weitzman footwear brand are expected to be flat from a year earlier.

Michael Kors Holdings * Says it will reduce promotional days during the holiday season by nearly two-thirds at its stores and website, and cut promotions by 67 days at department stores and off-price channels. (http://reut.rs/2iqSJJM) * Expects holiday quarter total revenue to be between $1.36 billion and $1.39 billion and diluted earnings per share in the range of $1.22 to $1.27 TJX Cos Inc * Says it has many initiatives underway to drive sales and traffic this holiday selling season and is in a 'terrific' inventory position. (http://reut.rs/2zIRHCx) * Expects holiday-quarter same-store sales growth of 1 to 2 percent.

(Compiled by Ahmed Farhatha, Sweta Singh and Uday Sampath in Bengaluru) ((UdaySampath.Kumar@thomsonreuters.com; Reuters Messaging: UdaySampath.Kumar.thomsonreuters.com@reuters.net))

Keywords: RETAIL OUTLOOK/Copyright (c) 2017 Thomson Reuters

BUZZ-U.S. STOCKS ON THE MOVE-Abercrombie & Fitch, Foot Locker, Splunk - 路透新闻

{{20171117T141615.706+0000}}BUZZ-U.S. STOCKS ON THE MOVE-Abercrombie & Fitch, Foot Locker, Splunk* Eikon search string for individual stock moves: [STXBZ]

* The Day Ahead newsletter: http://tmsnrt.rs/2ggOmBi

* The Morning News Call newsletter: http://tmsnrt.rs/2fwPLTh

UPDATE 4-J.B. Hunt, Wal-Mart climb aboard Tesla's electric truck - 路透新闻

{{20171117T131848.000+0000}}UPDATE 4-J.B. Hunt, Wal-Mart climb aboard Tesla's electric truckNov 17 (Reuters)

(Recasts throughout, adds context on regulatory pressure to cut diesel pollution)

By Arjun Panchadar and Eric M. Johnson

Nov 17 (Reuters) - Tesla Inc on Friday got high-profile orders from Wal-Mart Stores Inc and fleet operator J.B. Hunt for its future electric truck, but would-be customers indicated they are giving the big rig a try, not buying in volume.

Most of the customers who announced plans to put down $5,000 deposits for the Tesla Semi indicated they wanted to test a few of the vehicles. Wal-Mart said it plans to order a total of 15 Tesla trucks, five for the United States and ten for Canada. The company operates a fleet of about 6,000 trucks in the United States.

JB Hunt Transport Inc was the first major U.S. trucking company to announce an order for Tesla's new "Semi" electric trucks, saying it had reserved multiple vehicles for use on the U.S. West Coast. [nBw11VJ7Xa]

Hunt did not say how many of the vehicles it would reserve. Tesla unveiled the Semi on Thursday without specifying prices.[nL1N1NM1N4]

The early orders reflected the uncertainty about how the market for electric commercial vehicles will develop. About 260,000 Class-8 trucks are produced in North America annually, and that market has a value of about $28.6 billion, said Don Ake, vice president of commercial vehicles at FTR, an industry economics research firm.

The 500-mile (800 km) range between charges that Tesla Chief Executive Elon Musk promised on Thursday for the Tesla Semi is about half the range between fill-ups of a diesel Class 8 truck. Heavy batteries cut payload and add cost, potential deal killers for fleet buyers focused on operating cost per mile. [nL1N1NM1N4]

However, Tesla, and incumbent truck makers such as Daimler AG , Navistar International Corp and its partner Volkswagen AG are investing in electric trucks in a bet that the market will shift over the next decade.

For global truck makers, the biggest market for electric trucks will likely be China, where the government is moving aggressively to convert the transportation system to electrified vehicles.

Regulators around the world are ratcheting up pressure on the trucking industry to slash emissions of soot and carbon dioxide from diesel trucks. In the United States, the government has estimated that heavy-duty trucks represent 4 percent of vehicles on the road but account for 20 percent of carbon emissions. Under President Barack Obama, the United States required truck makers to boost fuel efficiency through 2027.

Separately, some cities and ports are discussing banning or heavily taxing diesel vehicles. The Ports of Los Angeles and Long Beach in Southern California have a goal of only having zero-emissions trucks by 2035. California is committing $140 million to subsidize low-carbon freight transportation.

Tesla has been trying to convince the trucking community that it can build an affordable electric big rig with the range and capacity to compete with relatively low-cost, time-tested diesel trucks.

It was not clear how many orders for Semis Tesla had in hand. Among companies announcing plans to acquire small numbers of Tesla trucks were Michigan retailer Meijer Inc [MEIJR.UL] and Canadian retail chain Loblaw , which has said it wants an entirely electric corporate vehicle fleet by 2030. [nL1N1NN1LM]

Some big logistics companies stayed on the sidelines. United Parcel Service Inc said the courier had nothing to announce regarding Tesla's vehicles but would always look for options that fit its needs.

Brad Pinchuk, chief executive of Dubuque, Iowa-based Hirschbach Motor Lines, said his firm was looking to test non-diesel big-rig options but needed longer ranges than Tesla could provide and speedier fuel-up times.

Pinchuk said he plans to buy two hydrogen-powered trucks made by Salt Lake City-based electric Nikola Motor Company when they are available in 2020.

"It's a different application – putting liquid hydrogen into tanks – so it will be very similar sort of situation to diesel," Pinchuk said. "You'd be able to fuel up. It would take about the same amount of time to fuel up a diesel and go about the same distance."

POINT MARCHÉS-Wall Street rebondit, tirée par Wal-Mart et Cisco - Reuters (French)

{{20171116T220918.109+0000}}POINT MARCHÉS-Wall Street rebondit, tirée par Wal-Mart et Cisco(Actualisé avec volumes, autres marchés)

* Le Dow a gagné 0,80%, le S&P-500 0,82%, le Nasdaq 1,30%

* Nouveau record pour le Nasdaq à plus de 6.800 points

* Wal-Mart gagne 10,9% et Cisco 5,2% après leurs résultats

* Le projet de réforme fiscale franchit une première haie

par Rodrigo Campos

NEW YORK, 16 novembre (Reuters) - La Bourse de New York est repartie de l'avant jeudi après deux séances de baisse, sous l'impulsion de Wal-Mart et de Cisco Systems dopés par leurs résultats trimestriels.

Le vote par la Chambre des représentants d'un projet de réforme fiscale a permis au marché d'accentuer son avance dans l'après-midi même si le texte, approuvé à une large majorité, doit encore franchir l'obstacle du Sénat où la majorité républicaine est plus mince. [nL8N1NM6XS]

L'indice Dow Jones <.DJI> a gagné 187,08 points, soit 0,80%, à 23.458,36 et l'indice S&P-500 <.SPX> a pris 21,02 points ou 0,82% à 2.585,64, revenant à 12 points de son record historique.

Il s'agit dans les deux cas de leur plus forte hausse en plus de deux mois.

Le Nasdaq Composite <.IXIC> a bondi de son côté de 87,08 points (1,30%) à 6.793,29, après un pic en séance à 6.806 points, au-delà de son précédent sommet du 7 novembre.

Wal-Mart s'est adjugé 10,90% à 99,62 dollars, de loin la meilleure performance du Dow Jones, après un record à 99,68. Le numéro un mondial de la grande distribution a enregistré au troisième trimestre la plus forte croissance de son chiffre d'affaires depuis 2009, avec un bond remarqué de ses ventes en ligne. [nL8N1NM4DO]

Cisco, l'équipementier des réseaux, a aussi soutenu le Dow avec une hausse de 5,19% à 35,88 dollars, profitant là encore de solides résultats et également de prévisions meilleures que prévu pour le trimestre en cours. Le titre a atteint en séance un pic de 36,67, du jamais vu depuis février 2001. [nL8N1NL7UU]

"Ces résultats sont une bonne nouvelle en ce qu'ils montrent que des sociétés traditionnelles comme Cisco et Wal-Mart s'adaptent à la nouvelle économie", commente Brian Battle, responsable du trading chez Performance Trust Capital Partners à Chicago. "Quant au vote sur la réforme fiscale, c'est loin d'être fait mais au moins la haie la plus basse est-elle franchie. Celle du Sénat sera plus haute."

L'indice Vix de la volatilité <.VIX>, qui mesure le coût de la protection contre une chute soudaine du S&P et fait figure à ce titre de baromètre de la peur à Wall Street, est retombé de 1,4 point à 11,76, sa première baisse en six jours.

Les volumes ont aussi diminué avec 6,31 milliards d'actions qui ont changé de mains, contre une moyenne de 6,81 milliards sur les 20 dernières séances.

VIACOM ET BEST BUY SANCTIONNÉS

Neuf des 11 grands indices sectoriels S&P ont fini en hausse, les seules baisses étant pour les valeurs de l'énergie <.SPNY> (-0,58%), plombées par un nouveau repli des cours du pétrole, et les services aux collectivités <.SPLRCU> (-0,40%), délaissés en raison de leur statut défensif.

Le marché a aussi salué les résultats du groupe agroalimentaire J M Smucker (+9,52%) mais a sanctionné ceux de Viacom , le propriétaire de la chaîne MTV (-3,78%), et du distributeur d'électronique Best Buy , victime du lancement tardif de l'iPhone X (-3,57%). [nL8N1NM44G]

Sur le front des fusions et acquisitions, le groupe de presse Time a bondi de 28% en réaction à une nouvelle approche de son concurrent Meredith tandis que le libraire Barnes & Noble , ciblé par un fonds activiste, a grimpé de 7,58%. [nL8N1NM717][nL8N1NM6W0]

Le rebond des marchés actions a été général avec l'indice MSCI Monde <.MIWD00000PUS> qui a regagné 0,8% après cinq séances consécutives de baisse et les Bourses européennes qui ont aussi repris des couleurs. [nL8N1NM6BW]

Le regain d'appétit pour le risque a soutenu le dollar, qui a repris 0,1% face à un panier de grandes devises après avoir touché la veille un creux depuis le 20 octobre.

L'euro/dollar s'est tassé de 0,2% à 1,1770.

Sur le marché obligataire, le rendement de l'emprunt de référence à 10 ans a progressé à 2,350% contre 2,335% mercredi et celui du papier à deux ans a atteint un pic de neuf ans à 1,716%, contre 1,691%.

L'écart de rendement entre le 2 ans et le 10 ans s'est réduit à 63,2 points de base , le plus serré depuis novembre 2007, reflétant les anticipations de nouvelles hausses de taux de la Réserve fédérale.

Le "spread" entre les rendements des emprunts à 5 ans et à 30 ans s'est lui contracté à 72,4 points de base, ce qui ne s'était plus vu depuis décembre 2011.

(avec Sruthi Shankar à Bangalore, Véronique Tison pour le service français) ((Service économique)(;)(tél 01 49 49 53 87)(;))Copyright (c) 2017 Thomson Reuters

GLOBAL MARKETS-Stocks, dollar climb as U.S. House OKs tax overhaul - 路透新闻

{{20171116T213846.261+0000}}GLOBAL MARKETS-Stocks, dollar climb as U.S. House OKs tax overhaul* Oil prices end lower

* Wall Street adds to gain after House tax overhaul vote

* Graphic: World FX rates in 2017 http://tmsnrt.rs/2egbfVh

(Updates with U.S. markets' closing levels)

By Caroline Valetkevitch

NEW YORK, Nov 16 (Reuters) - U.S. stocks rose and the dollar edged higher against a basket of major currencies on Thursday after the U.S. House of Representatives passed its version of a tax overhaul bill.

Earnings-related gains in Wal-Mart and Cisco also boosted stocks, and the MSCI index of world stocks <.MIWD00000PUS> rose after five consecutive daily losses.

The Dow Jones Industrial Average and the S&P 500 chalked up their biggest percentage gains in over two months.

The House approved a broad package of tax cuts affecting businesses, individuals and families, moving Republicans and President Donald Trump an important step closer to the biggest tax code overhaul in a generation. [nL1N1NM0PI]

The legislative battle now shifts to the Senate, where the Republican majority is much slimmer. Republicans can lose no more than two Senate votes and at least two GOP senators have already spoken against the Senate version of the bill.

"The tax plan isn't a foregone conclusion but it passed the lowest hurdle in the House," said Brian Battle, director of trading at Performance Trust Capital Partners in Chicago.

"The even higher hurdle is to have something pass in the Senate. The reconciliation will be the real measure if it happens," he said.

The dollar index <.DXY>, which hit 93.813 on Wednesday, its lowest since Oct. 20, was also supported by a general improvement in risk appetite across financial markets. The index was last up 0.1 percent.

The Dow <.DJI> rose 187.08 points, or 0.8 percent, to 23,458.36, the S&P 500 <.SPX> gained 21.02 points, or 0.82 percent, to 2,585.64 and the Nasdaq Composite <.IXIC> added 87.08 points, or 1.3 percent, to 6,793.29.

The pan-European FTSEurofirst 300 index <.FTEU3> rose 0.65 percent and MSCI's gauge of stocks across the globe <.MIWD00000PUS> gained 0.80 percent.

Oil prices extended their losing streak as rising U.S. production and inventories threatened to undermine a rally sparked by tightening world supply as a consequence of OPEC's curbs on output.

U.S. crude declined 19 cents to settle at $55.14 a barrel while Brent crude fell 51 cents to settle at $61.36.

U.S. Treasury two-year yields hit a nine-year high as risk appetite recovered globally and a batch of neutral to solid economic reports put the Federal Reserve on track to raise interest rates in 2018.

The rise in two-year yields pushed the curve to its flattest in a decade. The yield curve has declined for four straight days.

The gap between U.S. 2-year note and U.S. 10-year note yields contracted to 63.2 basis points m the tightest since November 2007. The gap was last at 65.1 basis points.

In late trading, the 10-year Treasury yield rose to 2.355 percent, from 2.335 percent late on Wednesday. U.S. two-year yields climbed to a nine-year peak of 1.716 percent, from 1.691 percent on Wednesday. Two-year yields were last at 1.712 percent.

By Caroline Valetkevitch

NEW YORK, Nov 16 (Reuters) - U.S. stocks rose and the dollar edged higher against a basket of major currencies on Thursday after the U.S. House of Representatives passed its version of a tax overhaul bill.

After five consecutive daily losses, the MSCI index of world stocks <.MIWD00000PUS> was up 0.8 percent, helped by U.S. stocks, which extended gains following the House vote. The Nasdaq hit a record high.

Stocks were already higher on earnings-related gains in Wal-Mart and Cisco .

US STOCKS-Wal-Mart, tech stocks lead Wall St gains - 路透新闻

{{20171116T175406.957+0000}}US STOCKS-Wal-Mart, tech stocks lead Wall St gains* Wal-Mart hits record high after results, boosts staples index

* Traders await vote on U.S. tax bill

* VIX posts first fall in six days

* Indexes up: Dow 0.86 pct, S&P 0.90 pct, Nasdaq 1.38 pct

(Updates to early afternoon)

By Sruthi Shankar

Nov 16 (Reuters) - Wall Street's main indexes marched higher on Thursday, driven by gains in Wal-Mart and technology shares, while investors awaited a vote on the Republican tax bill.

Wal-Mart surged as much as 9.10 percent to hit a record high of $98.01 after reporting U.S. same-store sales that beat expectations on hurricane-related purchases and soaring online sales. [nL1N1NM0OQ]

Cisco soared 6.3 percent after the company's profit forecast came in above estimates, boosting the S&P technology index <.SPLRCT>. [nL1N1NL2BD]

Gains in the session put the S&P and the Dow on course for their biggest percentage rise in more than two months.

"The bull market is still intact. Good earnings and strong economic data are what stocks care about," said Michael Antonelli, managing director, institutional sales trading at Robert W. Baird in Milwaukee.

"While tax debate is an important catalyst, it's not the only catalyst that moves market."

The Republican-controlled U.S. Congress is approaching a major test of its ability to overhaul tax code, as lawmakers prepare for their first full-scale vote on sweeping tax legislation.

U.S. House Speaker Paul Ryan told Fox News he was confident his chamber had the votes to pass its version of the plan. A vote was expected early on Thursday afternoon. [nL1N1NM0PI]

The CBOE Volatility index <.VIX>, Wall Street's fear gauge, posted its first decline in six days.

At 12:30 p.m. ET (1630 GMT), the Dow Jones Industrial Average <.DJI> was up 200.67 points, or 0.86 percent, at 23,471.95, the S&P 500 <.SPX> was up 22.97 points, or 0.90 percent, at 2,587.59 and the Nasdaq Composite <.IXIC> was up 92.31 points, or 1.38 percent, at 6,798.52.

Nine of the 11 major S&P indexes were higher, led by gains in consumer staples <.SPLRCS>. Utilities <.SPLRCU> and energy <.SPNY> sectors were the only laggards.

Folgers coffee maker J M Smucker rose nearly 10 percent as its sales and profit topped analysts' forecasts. [nL3N1NM446]

Viacom shares slipped 4.10 percent after the MTV owner said it expected high single-digit declines in revenue from U.S. cable TV operators and online distributors in the first half of 2018. [nL3N1NM448]

Best Buy fell 4.71 percent as same-store sales came in below estimates, hurt by a late launch of iPhone X. [nL3N1NM444]

Advancing issues outnumbered decliners on the NYSE by 2,279 to 583. On the Nasdaq, 2,309 issues rose and 550 fell.

UPDATE 4-Wal-Mart shares jump on strong U.S. sales growth - Reuters News

{{20171116T165042.898+0000}}UPDATE 4-Wal-Mart shares jump on strong U.S. sales growth(Updates shares, adds background and Breakingviews link,)

By Nandita Bose

CHICAGO, Nov 16 (Reuters) - Wal-Mart Stores Inc reported better-than-expected U.S. comparable sales on Thursday, as customers stocked up on food and other supplies ahead of hurricanes and online purchases soared, sending its shares up more than 8.5 percent.

The third quarter marked Wal-Mart's strongest U.S. sales growth since 2009 despite sluggish demand and competition from Amazon.com Inc that has hurt brick-and-mortar rivals. The retailer has notched more than three straight years of overall comparable sales growth. "Momentum in the business is really strong," Wal-Mart Chief Financial Officer Brett Biggs said on an earnings conference call.

Hurricane-related sales contributed 30 to 50 basis points to overall comparable sales, the world's largest retailer said, as Hurricanes Harvey and Irma spurred demand for food and grocery items as well as building materials.

"Food delivered its strongest quarterly performance in six years," Wal-Mart U.S. Chief Executive Greg Foran said.

Wal-Mart has invested in its online business, cut prices and improved its in-store shopping experience by raising worker wages and making stores cleaner and more efficient.

These investments weighed on operating margins and profit, however, which both fell compared to the year-ago quarter.

Online sales soared 50 percent, exceeding growth at other big retailers but coming in below the previous quarter's 60 percent surge.

Those sales added 80 basis points to the quarter's comparable sales gain, boosted by walmart.com, the retailer's online grocery delivery service and the acquisition of e-commerce startup Jet.com last year.

"Wal-Mart's online performance continues to validate its substantial investments in this critical channel," said Moody's retail analyst Charlie O'Shea.

Wal-Mart forecast strong performance in the key holiday quarter and raised its full-year profit forecast. It now expects earnings per share of $4.38 to $4.46 for the fiscal year versus $4.30 to $4.40 previously.

Rival Target Corp has also slashed prices and invested in its website and delivery, but has been less successful at translating that into sales and profit growth. Its holiday-quarter profit forecast fell short of analysts' expectations on Wednesday, sending shares down 10 percent.[nL3N1NL45J]

The holiday shopping season can account for as much as 40 percent of a retailers' annual sales. Wal-Mart has said it will double down on incentives and has tripled its online selections.

To compete with Amazon, Wal-Mart will offer free two-day shipping on more than two million products when the order exceeds $35 and discounts for online orders picked up at stores.

Excluding special items, earnings per share were $1 in the quarter ended Oct. 31, exceeding the average analyst estimate of 97 cents, according to Thomson Reuters I/B/E/S.

Operating income fell 6.9 percent, while operating margins slipped to 3.9 percent from 4.4 percent the same period a year earlier.

Sales at U.S. stores open at least a year rose 2.7 percent, excluding fuel price fluctuations, topping expectations for a rise of 1.7 percent, according to Consensus Metrix.

Net income dropped to $1.75 billion from $3.03 billion a year earlier due to a charge related to retiring higher-rate debt and exiting properties in international markets.

Wal-Mart said it was close to settling a years-long foreign-bribery probe and recorded a $283 million accrual charge related to a settlement.

Shares of Wal-Mart were last up 8.4 percent at $97.38. They have risen more than 30 percent so far this year.

^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^> (Reporting by Nandita Bose in Chicago; Editing by Jeffrey Benkoe and Meredith Mazzilli) ((nandita.bose@thomsonreuters.com; +13124088726; Reuters Messaging: nandita.bose.reuters.com@reuters.net))

US STOCKS-Gains in Wal-Mart, Cisco lift Wall Street - 路透新闻

{{20171116T162415.820+0000}}US STOCKS-Gains in Wal-Mart, Cisco lift Wall Street* Cisco, Wal-Mart shares boost Dow, S&P

* Tech stocks rebound

* Viacom slumps after weak forecast

* Indexes up: Dow 0.77 pct, S&P 0.76 pct, Nasdaq 1.17 pct

(Changes comment, updates prices, adds details on tax plan)

By Sruthi Shankar

Nov 16 (Reuters) - The S&P 500 index recovered from its worst two-day fall since August on Thursday after Wal-Mart and Cisco shares soared on strong results.

Wal-Mart surged 8.74 percent to hit a record high of $97.90 after reporting quarterly sales that beat expectations on hurricane-related purchases and soaring online sales. [nL1N1NM0OQ]

Cisco shares surged 6.44 percent as strength in security business helped its earnings. [nL1N1NL2BD] Both the stocks boosted the S&P and the Dow.

"The bull market is still intact. Good earnings and strong economic data are what stocks care about," said Michael Antonelli, managing director, institutional sales trading at Robert W. Baird in Milwaukee.

"While tax debate is an important catalyst, it's not the only catalyst that moves market."

The Republican-controlled U.S. Congress is approaching a major test of its ability to overhaul tax code, as lawmakers prepare for their first full-scale vote on sweeping tax legislation.

U.S. House Speaker Paul Ryan told Fox News he was confident his chamber had the votes to pass its version of the plan. A vote was expected early on Thursday afternoon. [nL1N1NM0PI]

At 10:45 a.m. ET (1445 GMT), the Dow Jones Industrial Average <.DJI> was up 178.42 points, or 0.77 percent, at 23,449.7, the S&P 500 <.SPX> was up 19.58 points, or 0.76 percent, at 2,584.2 and the Nasdaq Composite <.IXIC> was up 78.54 points, or 1.17 percent, at 6,784.75.

The CBOE Volatility index <.VIX>, Wall Street's fear gauge, posted its first decline in six days.

Nine of the 11 major S&P indexes were higher, led by gains in consumer staples <.SPLRCS> and technology stocks <.SPLRCT>.

Folgers coffee maker J M Smucker rose about 8.04 percent as its sales and profit topped analysts' forecasts. [nL3N1NM446]

Utilities <.SPLRCU> and energy <.SPNY> sectors were the only laggards.

Viacom shares sank 5.6 percent after the MTV owner said it expected high single-digit declines in revenue from U.S. cable TV operators and online distributors in the first half of 2018. [nL3N1NM448]

Best Buy fell 6.88 percent as quarterly same-store sales came in below estimates, hurt by a late launch of iPhone X. [nL3N1NM444]

Advancing issues outnumbered decliners on the NYSE by 2,235 to 537. On the Nasdaq, 2,214 issues rose and 513 fell.

ACTUALIZA 1-Ventas de Wal-Mart suben en tercer trimestre impulsadas por huracanes; acciones trepan - Reuters (Spanish)

{{20171116T153656.165+0000}}ACTUALIZA 1-Ventas de Wal-Mart suben en tercer trimestre impulsadas por huracanes; acciones trepan(Amplía información)

Por Nandita Bose

CHICAGO, 16 nov (Reuters) - Wal-Mart Stores Inc , la minorista más grande del mundo, reportó el jueves ventas trimestrales mejores a las esperadas en sus tiendas de Estados Unidos, impulsadas por compras ligadas a huracanes y un salto en el comercio online, lo que disparaba las acciones en más de 8 por ciento.

La cadena minorista ha registrado más de tres años consecutivos de crecimiento en las ventas comparables, algo que no ha logrado ninguna otra firma del sector, pese a una menor demanda y a un ambiente hostil que ha dañado a sus rivales.

"Tenemos impulso y es alentador ver a los consumidores responder en nuestras tiendas y a nuestras iniciativas de comercio electrónico", dijo el presidente ejecutivo de Wal-Mart, Doug McMillon.

Excluyendo ítems especiales, las ganancias por acción aumentaron a 1 dólar en el tercer trimestre finalizado el 31 de octubre, superando la estimación promedio de analistas de una utilidad de 97 centavos por papel, según Thomson Reuters I/B/E/S.

Las fuertes inversiones de la compañía en comercio online han tenido su costo. El ingreso operativo de Wal-Mart bajó un 6,9 por ciento a 4.760 millones de dólares. Los márgenes operativos retrocedieron al 3,9 por ciento desde un 4,4 por ciento en igual período del año previo.

Las ventas en las tiendas estadounidenses abiertas hace al menos un año aumentaron un 2,7 por ciento, excluyendo las fluctuaciones de precios de los combustibles. Analistas anticipaban un avance de 1,7 por ciento, según una encuesta de la firma Consesus Metrix.

Las ventas relacionadas con huracanes, sobre todo de alimentos, contribuyeron entre 30 a 50 puntos básicos a las comparaciones generales, dijo la compañía. 100 puntos base equivalen a un 1 por ciento. En agosto y septiembre, los devastadores Harvey e Irma dispararon la demanda de materiales para la prevención y reconstrucción, además de víveres.

Las ventas por internet se incrementaron un 50 por ciento durante el trimestre, excediendo las tasas de crecimiento de la industria, pero a un ritmo más lento que en el trimestre anterior, cuando subieron un 60 por ciento.

Wal-Mart aumentó su pronóstico de ganancias para todo el año. Ahora prevé utilidades por acción entre 4,38 y 4,46 dólares para el año fiscal, desde una proyección previa de 4,30 a 4,40 dólares.

Las acciones de la compañía trepaban un 8,1 por ciento a las 1510 GMT, a 97,11 dólares, tras cerrar a 89,83 dólares el miércoles. En lo que va del año los papeles de Wal-Mart han escalado más de 30 por ciento.

(Editado en español por Rodrigo Charme y Ana Laura Mitidieri) ((nandita.bose@thomsonreuters.com; +13124088726; Mesa de Edición en español +562 2437 44 00. Twitter: @ReutersLatam)) ((REUTERS RCH GB ALM SR))Copyright (c) 2017 Thomson Reuters

BOLSA EUA-Mercados se recuperam com resultados fortes do Wal-Mart e da Cisco - Reuters (Portuguese, Brazil)

{{20171116T152547.486+0000}}BOLSA EUA-Mercados se recuperam com resultados fortes do Wal-Mart e da Cisco16 Nov (Reuters) - Os mercados acionários norte-americanos se recuperavam de dois dias de quedas nesta quinta-feira depois que as ações do setor de tecnologia receberam um impulso dos resultados da Cisco e o Wal-Mart atingiu máxima recorde.

Às 13:25 (horário de Brasília), o índice Dow Jones <.DJI> subia 0,69 por cento, a 23.432 pontos, enquanto o S&P 500 <.SPX> ganhava 0,625044 por cento, a 2.581 pontos. O índice de tecnologia Nasdaq <.IXIC> avançava 0,95 por cento, a 6.770 pontos

As ações do Wal-Mart subiam 8 por cento depois que o maior varejista do mundo divulgou vendas trimestrais que superaram as expectativas, devido a compras relacionadas a furacões e ao aumento das vendas online. [nL1N1NM14E]

As ações da Cisco subiam 5,8 por cento uma vez que a força nos negócios de segurança ajudou seus resultados.

As ações dessas empresas impulsionavam o S&P e o Dow Jones.

"Uma das histórias mais notáveis deste ano é a do Wal-Mart e eles estão provando isso novamente com seus resultados hoje", disse o estrategista-chefe de mercado da B. Riley FBR, Art Hogan.

Nove dos 11 principais índices do S&P avançavam, impulsionados pelo índice de bens de consumo básicos <.SPLRCS> e pelo setor de tecnologia <.SPLRCT>.

UPDATE 2-Asda's stalling sales growth shows new boss' challenge - Reuters News

{{20171116T151014.351+0000}}UPDATE 2-Asda's stalling sales growth shows new boss' challenge* Third quarter underlying sales rise 1.1 pct

* Growth was 1.8 pct in previous quarter

* New CEO to start in January

* Shares in rivals rise

(Adds detail, Walmart quotes)

By James Davey

LONDON, Nov 16 (Reuters) - Sales growth at Asda, the British supermarket arm of Walmart , the world's largest retailer, slowed in its latest quarter, showing the tough task facing its new boss to rev-up its recovery in a cut-throat market.

Last month, Asda said Chief Executive Sean Clarke, a Walmart veteran of 21 years, would step down in January after just 18 months in the job and be replaced by head of operations Roger Burnley, a former Sainsbury's executive. [nL8N1N55E3]

Asda and its major rivals -- market leader Tesco , Sainsbury's and Morrisons -- are all grappling with the rapid growth of German discounters Aldi and Lidl.

They are also having to cope with more expensive food imports due to a weaker pound since Britain voted to leave the European Union, while consumer spending is under pressure from rising inflation, subdued wage growth and economic uncertainty.

Of Britain's major players analysts reckon Asda was hurt the most by the rise of the discounters as its traditional price advantage was eroded.

Walmart said in February it was too slow in starting the repositioning of Asda and had not focused enough on using its leverage as a parent so that its British arm could be more aggressive on price cuts. [nL5N1FS4I4]

Asda's like-for-like sales rose 1.1 percent in the three months to Sept. 30, its fiscal third quarter -- a second straight quarter of underlying sales growth after three years of sales falls but below the previous quarter's growth of 1.8 percent, which was boosted by Easter trading. [nL8N1L32YP]

Asda's gross profit rate declined in the quarter.

MORE WORK TO DO

"The improvements in store experience and price investments are increasing store basket sizes," said Walmart President and CEO Doug McMillon. Basket size increased 2.5 percent but customer traffic was down 1.4 percent.

Brett Biggs, Walmart's finance chief, said the parent was pleased with Asda's performance but said "we know we have more work to do."

Asda's comparative numbers were extremely weak - in the same quarter last year like-for-like sales slumped 5.8 percent. Also Asda would have benefited from food price inflation across the industry - running at 3.4 percent according to the latest industry data. [nL8N1NK3BC]

That data, published on Tuesday, also showed Asda recorded the lowest rate of sales growth of the big four in the 12 weeks to Nov.5.

Shares in Tesco, Sainsbury's and Morrisons were up 0.3, 1.1 and 1.6 percent respectively.

Last week, Marks & Spencer said its food business faced "stronger headwinds" and would slow openings of its convenience stores, while Sainsbury's said shoppers were currently "very value conscious". [nL5N1NE1TD] [nL8N1NF3F3]

On Thursday, official data showed British retail sales volumes fell 0.3 percent year-on-year in October -- the biggest decline since March 2013. [nL8N1NM2Q2]

Clarke and Burnley have focused their turnaround efforts on re-establishing Asda's competitiveness by sharpening pricing in key areas such as fresh meat and vegetables, improving the quality and availability of product ranges and making its stores more attractive. Like rivals they are attacking costs. In September Asda cut 300 head office jobs. [nL8N1LN4XQ]

"The market environment will continue to be challenging into next year but we're well placed with clear plans," Clarke said.

Separately on Thursday Walmart reported better-than-expected quarterly sales. [nL1N1NM0OQ]

(Editing by Kate Holton and Jane Merriman) ((james.davey@thomsonreuters.com; +44 20 7542 7674; Reuters Messaging: james.davey.thomsonreuters.com@reuters.net))

Vendas do Wal-Mart no 3ºtri ganham impulso de furacões nos EUA e comércio eletrônico - Reuters (Portuguese, Brazil)

{{20171116T150803.662+0000}}Vendas do Wal-Mart no 3ºtri ganham impulso de furacões nos EUA e comércio eletrônicoCHICAGO, Estados Unidos, 16 Nov (Reuters) - O Wal-Mart Stores , maior varejista do mundo, informou vendas trimestrais melhores do que o esperado no conceito mesmas lojas nos Estados Unidos nesta quinta-feira, impulsionadas por compras relacionadas aos furacões Harvey e Irma nos Estados Unidos, e por aumento de vendas online.

A varejista tem registrado mais de três anos consecutivos de crescimento de vendas comparáveis, apesar da lenta demanda e um difícil ambiente de varejo que prejudicou os rivais de lojas físicas.

Excluindo itens especiais, o lucro por ação chegou a 1 dólar no terceiro trimestre encerrado em 31 de outubro, excedendo a estimativa média de analistas de 0,97 dólar, de acordo com a Thomson Reuters I/B/E/S.

O lucro operacional da empresa caiu 6,9 por cento para 4,76 bilhões de dólares. As margens operacionais caíram para 3,9 por cento, ante 4,4 por cento no mesmo período do ano anterior.

As vendas nas lojas dos EUA abertas há pelo menos um ano aumentaram 2,7 por cento, excluindo as flutuações de preços dos combustíveis. Resultado mais forte do que as expectativas do mercado, de um aumento de 1,7 por cento, segundo a Consensus Metrix.

As vendas online subiram 50 por cento durante o trimestre, superando taxas de crescimento na indústria, mas o ritmo foi mais lento em relação ao aumento de 60 por cento verificado no trimestre anterior. A empresa adicionou 80 pontos base ao ganho de vendas comparável ao terceiro trimestre, impulsionado pela aquisição da startup de comércio eletrônico Jet.com por 3,3 bilhões de dólares no ano passado.

"O desempenho online da Wal-Mart continua a validar seus investimentos substanciais neste canal crítico", disse Charlie O'Shea, analista de varejo da Moody's.

O Wal-Mart vem investindo agressivamente no comércio eletrônico desde 2016 e agora vende mais de 60 milhões de itens online. A varejista oferece entrega gratuita de dois dias sem taxas de adesão para competir contra a Amazon e descontos em compras online.

A empresa também aumentou previsão de lucro para todo o ano. Agora, espera que o lucro por ação seja de 4,38 a 4,46 dólares, ante perspectiva anterior de 4,30 a 4,40 dólares.

(Por Nandita Bose)

((Tradução Redação São Paulo; +55 11 56447745))

US STOCKS-Wall St recovers on strong Wal-Mart, Cisco earnings - 路透新闻

{{20171116T150516.206+0000}}US STOCKS-Wall St recovers on strong Wal-Mart, Cisco earnings* Cisco, Wal-Mart shares boost Dow, S&P

* Tech stocks rebound

* Indexes up: Dow 0.55 pct, S&P 0.44 pct, Nasdaq 0.72 pct

(Updates to open)

By Sruthi Shankar

Nov 16 (Reuters) - U.S. stock indexes recovered from two days of losses on Thursday after technology stocks got a boost from Cisco results and Wal-Mart soared to a record high.

Shares of Wal-Mart rose 7 percent after the world's largest retailer reported quarterly sales that beat expectations on hurricane-related purchases and soaring online sales. [nL1N1NM0OQ]

Cisco shares surged 6.7 percent as strength in security business helped its earnings. [nL1N1NL2BD]

Both the stocks powered the S&P 500 and the Dow Jones indexes.

"One of the most remarkable stories of this year is Wal-Mart and they are again proving that with their results today," said Art Hogan, chief market strategist at B. Riley FBR in Boston.

The S&P 500 recorded its biggest percentage decline in more than 2 months on Wednesday as energy stocks dropped on sliding crude prices and concerns over the passage of a tax revamp after two Republican senators were critical of the proposal weighed.

The Republican-controlled U.S. Congress is approaching a major test of its ability to overhaul tax code on Thursday, as lawmakers prepared for their first full-scale vote on sweeping tax legislation. [nL1N1NL2EH]

At 9:50 a.m. ET (1350 GMT), the Dow Jones Industrial Average <.DJI> was up 127.36 points, or 0.55 percent, at 23,398.64, the S&P 500 <.SPX> was up 11.39 points, or 0.44 percent, at 2,576.01 and the Nasdaq Composite <.IXIC> was up 48.38 points, or 0.72 percent, at 6,754.58.

Nine of the 11 major S&P indexes were higher, led by gains in consumer staples <.SPLRCS> and technology stocks <.SPLRCT>.

Folgers coffee maker J M Smucker rose about 6 percent, while Viacom slipped 8.25 percent after reporting results. [nL3N1NL580] [nL3N1NM43S]

Best Buy fell 6.61 percent as quarterly same-store sales came in below estimates, hurt by a late launch of iPhone X. [nL3N1NM444]

Advancing issues outnumbered decliners on the NYSE by 1,900 to 774. On the Nasdaq, 1,878 issues rose and 598 fell.

POINT MARCHÉS-Wall Street rebondit, record pour Wal-Mart - Reuters (French)

{{20171116T145928.503+0000}}POINT MARCHÉS-Wall Street rebondit, record pour Wal-Mart16 novembre (Reuters) - La Bourse de New York rebondit jeudi en début de séance au lendemain du repli le plus marqué subi par l'indice phare S&P 500 depuis septembre, une inversion de tendance favorisée par un regain d'appétit général pour le risque et de bons résultats d'entreprises.

L'indice Dow Jones <.DJI> gagne 132,54 points, soit 0,57%, à 23.403,82. Le Standard & Poor's 500 <.SPX>, plus large, progresse de 0,45% à 2.576,28 et le Nasdaq Composite <.IXIC> prend 0,76% à 6.756,92.

Wal-Mart Stores grimpe de 6,87% et a atteint un plus haut historique à 96,01 dollars après ses résultats trimestriels, marqués par une progression de ses ventes à périmètre constant pour un 13e trimestre consécutif sur la période août-octobre. [nL8N1NM3WA]

"L'une des plus remarquables histoires cette année est Wal-Mart et il le prouve encore avec ses résultats aujourd'hui", estime Art Hogan, responsable de la stratégie chez B. Riley FBR. En intégrant la hausse du jour, le titre gagne plus de 35% depuis le début de l'année.

Le secteur des biens de consommation courante <.SPLRCS> en profite et prend 1%.

Les publications trimestrielles de Cisco Systems - qui dispute à Wal-Mart la plus forte hausse du Dow Jones - et de JM Smucker sont également bien accueillies puisque les deux titres avancent respectivement de 6,94% et de 5,72%. [nL8N1NL7UU]

En revanche, Viacom chute de 7,76%, ses prévisions pour le premier semestre 2018 ayant déçu le marché. Best Buy cède 7,09% après la hausse plus faible que prévu de ses ventes à magasins comparables sur le dernier trimestre clos. [nL8N1NM44G]

Aux fusions et acquisitions, Rockwell Automation grimpe de 5,52% après le relèvement de l'offre d'achat d'Emerson Electric à environ 29 milliards de dollars (22,9 milliards d'euros), après le rejet de sa précédente proposition qui valorisait le fabricant d'équipements industriels à 27,6 milliards. [nL8N1NM4OF]

DES INDICATEURS MOINS BONS QUE PRÉVU

Les investisseurs restent attentifs à l'évolution des débats sur le projet de réforme fiscale, dont le retard voire une possible annulation inquiète le marché depuis plusieurs semaines.

A l'issue d'une rencontre avec Donald Trump, les élus républicains de la Chambre des représentants devraient voter aujourd'hui sur leur version du texte, qui prévoit notamment de ramener le taux d'imposition des entreprises de 35% à 20%.

Au chapitre économique, le nombre des inscriptions hebdomadaires au chômage ont augmenté de manière inattendue la semaine dernière aux Etats-Unis, l'amélioration du traitement des demandes de Porto Rico se poursuivant, mais la tendance de fond montre que les conditions du marché de l'emploi restent tendues. [nL8N1NM40L]

L'enquête de conjoncture mensuelle de la Réserve fédérale de Philadelphie montre par ailleurs que la croissance de l'activité économique dans le nord-est des Etats-Unis a ralenti plus fortement que prévu en novembre. [nZON025S05] Quant aux prix à l'importation, ils ont moins augmenté que prévu en octobre. [nL8N1NM4UY]

L'indice dollar a effacé ses gains après ses publications pour revenir à l'équilibre face à un panier de devises de référence <.DXY>. Parallèlement, l'euro recule de 0,1% face au dollar, sous 1,1780.

Les cours du pétrole sont orienté à la baisse mais l'approche de la réunion de l'Opep, qui devrait prolonger l'accord de limitation de l'offre le 30 novembre, pourrait limiter le repli.

Les indices boursiers européens évoluent en nette progression au moment de l'ouverture à Wall Street, aidés par le repli de l'euro: le Stoxx 600 <.STOXX> prend 0,7% et le CAC 40 <.FCHI> à Paris 0,63%.

LEAD 2-Wal-Mart-Ventes meilleures que prévu, l'action grimpe - Reuters (French)

{{20171116T144206.449+0000}}LEAD 2-Wal-Mart-Ventes meilleures que prévu, l'action grimpe(Actualisé avec commentaires, précisions, cours de Bourse)

CHICAGO, 16 novembre (Reuters) - Wal-Mart Stores a publié jeudi des ventes à périmètre constant meilleures qu'attendu au troisième trimestre, soutenues par les achats liés aux ouragans et de solides ventes en ligne.

L'action du géant américain de la distribution, qui a gagné plus de 30% depuis le début de l'année, prend 6,37% à 95,55 dollars dans les premiers échanges à Wall Street.

Wal-Mart a désormais enregistré plus de trois années consécutives de croissance de ses ventes, en dépit de conditions de marché difficiles pour les distributeurs traditionnels.

"Nous avons une bonne dynamique et c'est encourageant de voir nos clients réagir aux initiatives que nous prenons dans nos magasins et dans le commerce en ligne", a déclaré le directeur général Doug McMillon.

Hors éléments exceptionnels, le bénéfice ressort à un dollar par action sur la période août-octobre, contre 97 cents attendus par les analystes selon le consensus Thomson Reuters I/B/E/S.

Le bénéfice d'exploitation a baissé de 6,9% à 4,76 milliards de dollars et la marge d'exploitation s'est repliée à 3,9% contre 4,4% un an plus tôt, en raison des lourds investissements destinés à développer les ventes sur internet.

Les ventes des magasins Wal-Mart ouverts depuis au moins un an aux Etats-Unis ont augmenté de 2,7%, hors carburants, alors que les analystes s'attendaient à une progression limitée à 1,7%, selon le cabinet Consensus Metrix.

Les ouragans Harvey et Irma ont dopé la demande de matériaux de construction et de produits alimentaires. Ces ventes ont contribué à hauteur de 30 à 50 points de base (pdb) à la hausse globale des ventes au troisième trimestre.

Les ventes en ligne ont bondi de 50% sur la période, une croissance supérieure à l'ensemble du secteur, même si elle est inférieure au taux de 60% enregistré au deuxième trimestre. Elles ont contribué à hauteur de 80 pdb à la hausse des ventes.

"Les performances de l'activité en ligne de Wal Mart continuent à justifier les gros investissements réalisés à cette période charnière", dit l'analyste de Moody's Charlie O'Shea.

Wal-Mart investit massivement dans l'e-commerce depuis un an et propose désormais plus de 60 millions de produits en ligne. Le groupe offre la livraison gratuite en deux jours sans frais d'abonnement pour faire face à la concurrence d'Amazon et des rabais pour les clients qui viennent chercher leurs achats réalisés sur internet. Wal-Mart a acquis plusieurs start-up en vue d'attirer les clients plus jeunes.

Wal-Mart a également relevé sa prévision de bénéfice annuel, anticipant désormais un bénéfice par action compris entre 4,38 et 4,46 dollars pour l'exercice fiscal en cours, contre une prévision précédente de 4,30 à 4,40 dollars.

Mercredi, Target a annoncé une prévision de bénéfice ajusté pour la période des fêtes inférieure aux attentes des analystes. Le titre a fini en baisse de plus de 8%.

(Nandita Bose; Bertrand Boucey et Catherine Mallebay-Vacqueur et Juliette Rouillon pour le service français, édité par Wilfrid Exbrayat) ((paris.equities@reuters.com; Service économie, +33 1 49 49 53 87;))Copyright (c) 2017 Thomson Reuters

USA-Les valeurs à suivre à Wall Street (actualisé) - Reuters (French)

{{20171116T140353.813+0000}}USA-Les valeurs à suivre à Wall Street (actualisé)(Actualisé avec précisions sur Emerson Electric/Rockwell Automation et cours d'avant-Bourse)

NEW YORK, 16 novembre (Reuters) - Principales valeurs à suivre jeudi à Wall Street où les contrats à terme sur les indices de référence indiquent une ouverture en hausse de 0,3% à 0,4%:

* WAL-MART STORES - Le titre grimpe de 4,5% dans les échanges en avant-Bourse après la publication des résultats trimestriels du groupe. Le numéro un mondial de la distribution a annoncé une nouvelle hausse trimestrielle de ses ventes à magasins comparables, la treizième d'affilée, grâce à une augmentation de la fréquentation de ses magasins et des achats en ligne. [nL8N1NM4DO]

* CISCO SYSTEMS - Le titre grimpe de plus de 7% dans les transactions en avant-Bourse en réaction à la publication des résultats et prévisions du premier équipementier de réseaux mondial. Plusieurs intermédiaires ont relevé leur objectif de cours sur la valeur, qui a gagné 13% entre le début de l'année et la clôture de mercredi. [nL8N1NL7UU]

* EMERSON ELECTRIC a relevé jeudi son offre d'achat de ROCKWELL AUTOMATION à environ 29 milliards de dollars (22,9 milliards d'euros), après le rejet de sa précédente proposition, qui valorisait le fabricant américain d'équipements industriels à 27,6 milliards mais que celui-ci avait jugée insuffisante. Le titre Rockwell Automation grimpe de 4,1% dans les échanges en avant-Bourse. [nL8N1NM4OF]

* BEST BUY - Le distributeur de produits d'électronique grand public a fait état jeudi d'une progression moins élevée qu'attendu de ses ventes à magasins comparables au troisième trimestre, en raison du lancement tardif de l'iPhone X et des ouragans qui ont frappé les Etats-Unis, et ses prévisions pour la période des fêtes de fin d'année sont inférieures au consensus de Wall Street. Le titre reculait ensuite de 7,4% en avant-Bourse. [nL8N1NM44G]

* MATTEL a rejeté la dernière proposition d'achat de son concurrent HASBRO , ont déclaré mercredi des sources proches du dossier. L'action Mattel recule de 3,6% dans les transactions en avant-Bourse en réaction à cette information. Le titre Hasbro a perdu 1,2% dans les échanges en après-Bourse. [nL8N1NL7VQ]

* TIME serait de nouveau en discussions en vue de se vendre au groupe de médias MEREDITH CORP , qui disposerait cette fois du soutien financier des milliardaires David et Charles Koch, d'après le New York Times. L'action bondit de 11% en avant-Bourse.

* PROCTER & GAMBLE - L'investisseur activiste Nelson Peltz a annoncé qu'il avait remporté un siège au conseil d'administration après un nouveau décompte des voix, ce que le groupe de produits de grande consommation réfute pour le moment. Le titre gagne 2% dans les transactions en avant-Bourse.

* SCRIPPS NETWORKS INTERACTIVE - La division commerciale de la BBC envisage une offre de 500 millions de livres (560 millions d'euros) sur le télédiffuseur UKTV, une coentreprise qu'elle détient à parité avec le télédiffuseur américain, rapporte le Daily Telegraph, citant des sources. [nL8N1NL81R]

* T-MOBILE a annoncé jeudi qu'il proposerait un programme de rachats d'actions "significatif" qui pourrait débuter en décembre. L'opérateur mobile a également annoncé le lancement de la 5G sur tout le territoire américain d'ici 2020.

* VIACOM , propriétaire entre autres de la chaîne de télévision MTV et du studio de cinéma Paramount, a fait état jeudi d'un chiffre d'affaires trimestriel meilleur que prévu, la hausse des revenus issus de sa division cinématographique ayant contrebalancé le repli des redevances versées par les câblo-opérateurs et les distributeurs de contenus en ligne. Le titre gagne 1,8% en avant-Bourse.

* JM SMUCKER , le groupe agroalimentaire, qui fabrique entre autres le café Folgers, a fait état jeudi d'un chiffre d'affaires et de résultats supérieurs aux attentes au titre de son deuxième trimestre, grâce aux réductions de coûts et à la hausse des prix de certains produits comme le beurre de cacahuètes Jif. L'action monte de 5% en avant-Bourse.

* GAP publiera ses résultats du troisième trimestre après la clôture.

* MAXWELL TECHNOLOGIES - Le titre bondit de près de 7% en avant-Bourse alors que Franz Fink, le PDG du fabricant de composants pour le stockage d'énergie, a annoncé avoir racheté 230.000 actions pour 1,1 million de dollars.

* AXOGEN - L'action du fabricant de matériel chirurgical chute de plus de 11% à 22 dollars en avant-Bourse en raison d'un placement de titres sur le marché.

* CONSTELLIUM - Le titre du groupe spécialisé dans la fabrication de produits en aluminium s'envole de 17% en avant-Bourse; Morgan Stanley a relevé sa recommandation à "surpondérer" contre "pondération en ligne".

* PANDORA MEDIA - L'action gagne 5,9% en avant-Bourse à la faveur du relèvement de recommandation de BMO à "surperformance".
