BREAKINGVIEWS-Wal-Mart flexes its muscle in Amazon fight - Reuters Breakingviews

{{20171116T133840.582+0000}}BREAKINGVIEWS-Wal-Mart flexes its muscle in Amazon fight(The author is a Reuters Breakingviews columnist. The opinions expressed are her own.)

By Jennifer Saba

NEW YORK, Nov 16 (Reuters Breakingviews) - Wal-Mart is flexing its muscle in its fight with e-commerce giant Amazon . The $268 billion retailer increased its third-quarter revenue as more people visited its stores. Online, the firm kicked out impressive growth and even grocery sales improved. The Bentonville, Arkansas giant is worth keeping an eye on in Seattle.

The recent hurricanes in Texas and Florida drove more people to Wal-Mart to stock up on supplies and shore up against the storms. Even so, the growth in the top line – up more than 4 percent year-over-year to some $123 billion – came ahead of analysts' expectations of $121 billion.

Wal-Mart also notched some nice gains in its grocery business just as Amazon digests its $13.7 billion purchase of supermarket chain Whole Foods. That category delivered its strongest quarterly sales performance on a like-for-like basis in nearly six years partly due to Wal-Mart rolling out boss Doug McMillon's strategy of getting customers to buy online but pick up goods in stores. It even managed to surpass expectations with e-commerce sales, which soared 50 percent in the quarter. Moody's noted that was well ahead of its stated target of 40 percent.

Wal-Mart and Amazon are beginning to look alike on another front too: costs. Gross profit margins slipped 29 basis points at Wal-Mart to 25 percent as it ramps up aggressive pricing to better compete.

There, though, Wal-Mart can rely on some old-school skills. During an investor day in October, executives highlighted how they plan to control expenses as they spiff up stores and invest in online by applying zero-based budgeting at some of its divisions. A simple change in plastic bags produced $20 million in annualized savings, while shortening receipts returned some $7 million. The eye on the bottom line will keep the battle with Amazon chief Jeff Bezos interesting.

On Twitter https://twitter.com/jennifersaba

CONTEXT NEWS

- Wal-Mart's total revenue for the third quarter rose 4.2 percent year-over-year to $123.2 billion, the U.S. retailer said on Nov. 16. Earnings were $1.7 billion, or 58 cents per share, compared with $3 billion, or 98 cents per share, for the same period last year.

- U.S. sales, comparing like with like, increased 2.7 percent from a year earlier, while e-commerce sales grew 50 percent.

- Wal-Mart raised its full-year adjusted earnings per share forecast to between $4.38 and $4.46, from a previous range of $4.30 to $4.40.

Wal-Mart увеличил сопоставимые продажи 13-й квартал подряд, превысил прогнозы - Reuters (Russian)

{{20171116T124710.307+0000}}Wal-Mart увеличил сопоставимые продажи 13-й квартал подряд, превысил прогнозыЧИКАГО, 16 ноя (Рейтер) - Крупнейший в мире ритейлер Wal-Mart Stores Inc сообщил о росте сопоставимых продаж 13-й квартал подряд за счёт увеличения числа покупателей в магазинах и на онлайн-площадке.

Продажи в магазинах в США, работающих по меньшей мере год, выросли на 2,7 процента, исключая топливные расходы, в третьем квартале, завершившемся 31 октября. Аналитики ожидали, что увеличение составит 1,7 процента, согласно опросу исследовательской фирмы Consensus Metrix. Ритейлер фиксирует рост более трёх лет подряд, выделяясь на фоне конкурентов.

Скорректированная прибыль на акцию увеличилась до $1 против прогноза на уровне $0,97 на акцию.

Онлайн-продажи подскочили на 50 процентов за квартал, превысив общий рост отрасли, однако замедлились к предыдущему кварталу, когда они увеличились на 60 процентов.

Ventas comparables de Wal-Mart en tercer trimestre superan las estimaciones - Reuters (Spanish)

{{20171116T124502.995+0000}}Ventas comparables de Wal-Mart en tercer trimestre superan las estimacionesCHICAGO, 16 nov (Reuters) - Wal-Mart Stores Inc , la minorista más grande del mundo, reportó el jueves un decimotercer aumento consecutivo en sus ventas comparables trimestrales, impulsadas por un alza en la cantidad de compradores que visitaron sus tiendas y que realizaron compras por internet. Las ventas en las tiendas estadounidenses abiertas hace al menos un año aumentaron un 2,7 por ciento en el tercer trimestre terminado el 31 de octubre, excluyendo combustibles. Analistas anticipaban un avance de 1,7 por ciento, según una encuesta de la firma Consesus Metrix. La minorista ha registrado más de tres años consecutivos de crecimiento, algo que no ha logrado ninguna otra firma del sector. Las ganancias ajustadas por acción aumentaron a 1 dólar, superando las expectativas de analistas de 97 centavos por papel. Las ventas por internet se incrementaron un 50 por ciento durante el trimestre, excediendo las tasas de crecimiento de la industria, pero a un ritmo más lento que en el trimestre anterior, cuando subieron un 60 por ciento.

(Reporte de Nandita Bose en Chicago. Editado en español por Rodrigo Charme) ((nandita.bose@thomsonreuters.com; +13124088726; Mesa de Edición en español +562 2437 44 00. Twitter: @ReutersLatam)) ((REUTERS RCH GB))Copyright (c) 2017 Thomson Reuters

EARNINGS-TICKER-Manchester United steigert Umsatz und Gewinn  - Reuters (German)

{{20171116T123333.866+0000}}EARNINGS-TICKER-Manchester United steigert Umsatz und Gewinn Frankfurt, 16. Nov (Reuters) - Zahlreiche Firmen veröffentlichen dieser Tage ihre aktuelle Quartalsbilanz. Es folgt in Kurzform ein Überblick über einige Ergebnisse vom Donnerstag:

MANCHESTER UNITED: Der englische Fußballclub hat seinen operativen Gewinn im vergangenen Quartal um mehr als 17 Prozent auf 36,6 Millionen Pfund gesteigert. Der Umsatz kletterte um 15 Prozent auf 141 Millionen Pfund. Der Traditionsverein profitierte von starken TV-Einnahmen und seiner Teilnahme am lukrativen europäischen Wettbewerb Champions League.

WAL-MART: Der weltgrößte Einzelhandelskonzern hat im dreizehnten Quartal in Folge seinen Umsatz auf vergleichbarer Basis gesteigert. Dank mehr Kundschaft in den Läden und einer Verdopplung des Online-Geschäfts kletterte der Umsatz auf 123 (Vorjahr 118) Milliarden Dollar. Das übertraf die Erwartungen der Analysten.

ILIAD: Der Telekomkonzern, der sich mit Bouygues und Orange ein hartes Rennen liefert, kommt bei den Kunden an. Der Umsatz legte im dritten Quartal um 5,3 Prozent auf 1,25 Milliarden Euro zu. Die Zahl der Neukunden im Mobilfunkgeschäft lag bei 250.000.

BOUYGUES: Der Mischkonzern profitiert von guten Geschäften der Telekomsparte. Das Betriebsergebnis legte in den ersten drei Quartalen um 37 Prozent zu auf 976 Millionen Euro, der Umsatz stieg drei Prozent auf 23,8 Milliarden Euro.

PRUDENTIAL: Der britische Lebensversicherer sieht Chancen in der Verrentung der Babyboomer in den USA, der wachsenden Mittelschicht in Asien und den Marktentwicklungen in Europa. Der Gewinn legte in den ersten neun Monaten um 17 Prozent auf umgerechnet 2,76 Milliarden Euro zu.

VTG: Das Bahn-Logistikunternehmen blickt wegen Verzögerungen bei der geplanten Übernahme der Nacco-Gruppe etwas pessimistischer in die Zukunft. Der Gewinn werde im Gesamtjahr deswegen am unteren Ende der Spanne von 330 bis 360 Millionen Euro liegen. In den ersten neun Monaten verdiente das Unternehmen vor Zinsen, Steuern und Abschreibungen mit 250,7 Millionen Euro etwas weniger als vor Jahresfrist, der Umsatz legte dagegen dank einer hohen Nachfrage nach Waggons um gut acht Millionen auf 750,2 Millionen Euro zu.

(Zusammengestellt in den Redaktionen Berlin und Frankfurt. Bei Rückfragen wenden Sie sich bitte an die Redaktionsleitung unter den Telefonnummern +49 69 7565 1232 oder +49 30 2888 5168.)Copyright (c) 2017 Thomson Reuters

Wal-Mart, vendite comparabili trim3 crescono oltre attese  - Reuters (Italian)

{{20171116T122551.900+0000}}Wal-Mart, vendite comparabili trim3 crescono oltre attese CHICAGO, 16 novembre (Reuters) - Walmart il più grande gruppo di vendita al dettaglio del mondo, annuncia il tredicesimo trimestre consecutivo di aumento delle vendite comparabili, grazie al maggiore numero di clienti in negozio e online.

Le vendite nei centri aperti in Usa da almeno un anno sono cresciute del 2,7%, escludendo il carburante, nel terzo trimestre che si chiude il 31 ottobre.

Gli analisti avevano previsto un incremento dell'1,7% secondo un sondaggio condotto dalla società di ricerca Consesus Metrix. Il gruppo è l'unico nel suo settore ad aver messo a segno più di tre anni consecutivi di crescita.

L'utile per azione adjusted è salito a un dollaro, oltre le stime per 97 cent.

Le vendite online si sono impennate del 50% nel trimestre, un ritmo di crescita superiore a quello del settore, ma più lento dell'incremento del 60% del trimestre precedente.

Il titolo balza del 3,1% nel preborsa.

Les ventes de Wal-Mart dépassent les attentes - Reuters (French)

{{20171116T122356.618+0000}}Les ventes de Wal-Mart dépassent les attentesCHICAGO, 16 novembre (Reuters) - Wal-Mart Stores a vu ses ventes à périmètre constant progresser pour un 13e trimestre consécutif sur la période août-octobre, avec une hausse de la fréquentation de ses magasins et des achats en ligne.

L'action du géant américain de la distribution a pris 3,1% dans les transactions avant l'ouverture à Wall Street après la publication de ses résultats trimestriels jeudi.

Les ventes dans les magasins Wal-Mart ouverts depuis au moins un an aux Etats-Unis ont augmenté de 2,7%, hors carburant, alors que les analystes s'attendaient à une progression limitée à 1,7%, selon le cabinet Consensus Metrix.

Wal-Mart a désormais enregistré plus de trois années consécutives de croissance de ses ventes, plus que tout autre distributeur aux Etats-Unis.

Le bénéfice ajusté par action a lui aussi été supérieur aux attentes, à 1,00 dollar contre 97 cents anticipé par les analystes.

Les ventes en ligne ont bondi de 50% sur la période, une croissance supérieure à celle de l'ensemble du secteur, même si elle est légèrement inférieure au taux de 60% enregistré sur les trois mois précédents.

(Nandita Bose; Bertrand Boucey pour le service français) ((paris.equities@reuters.com; Service économie, +33 1 49 49 53 87;))Copyright (c) 2017 Thomson Reuters

Sales growth at Walmart's Asda slows in latest quarter - Reuters News

{{20171116T121821.985+0000}}Sales growth at Walmart's Asda slows in latest quarterLONDON, Nov 16 (Reuters) - Asda, the British supermarket arm of Walmart , the world's largest retailer, on Thursday reported a slowdown in its rate of sales growth despite industry inflation and very weak comparative numbers.

Asda, the UK's third largest grocer after market leader Tesco and No. 2 Sainsbury's , said like-for-like sales rose 1.1 percent in the three months to Sept. 30, its fiscal third quarter.

That compared to a rise of 1.8 percent in the previous quarter and marked the second straight quarter of underlying sales growth. Prior to that it had endured three years of sales falls. [nL8N1L32YP]

Comparative numbers were extremely weak - in the same period last year like-for-like sales slumped 5.8 percent. Asda would also have benefited from food price inflation across the industry - running at 3.4 percent according to the latest industry data. [nL8N1NK3BC]

"While the business has improved, we still have more work to do," said parent Walmart.

(Reporting by James Davey; editing by Kate Holton) ((james.davey@thomsonreuters.com; +44 20 7542 7674; Reuters Messaging: james.davey.thomsonreuters.com@reuters.net))

Wal-Mart's third-quarter comparable sales beat estimates - Reuters News

{{20171116T121315.588+0000}}Wal-Mart's third-quarter comparable sales beat estimatesCHICAGO, Nov 16 (Reuters) - Wal-Mart Stores Inc , the world's largest retailer, reported its 13th consecutive rise in quarterly comparable sales on Thursday, driven by an increase in the number of shoppers who visited stores and online purchases.

Sales at U.S. stores open at least a year rose 2.7 percent, excluding fuel, in the third quarter ended Oct. 31. Analysts forecast a gain of 1.7 percent, according to a poll by research firm Consesus Metrix. The retailer has recorded more than three straight years of growth, unmatched by any other retailer.

Adjusted earnings per share increased to $1, beating expectations of 97 cents per share.

Online sales soared 50 percent during the quarter, exceeding growth rates in the industry, but slower from the previous quarter's 60 percent rise.

(Reporting by Nandita Bose in Chicago; Editing by Jeffrey Benkoe) ((nandita.bose@thomsonreuters.com; +13124088726; Reuters Messaging: nandita.bose.reuters.com@reuters.net))

Guten Morgen von Reuters am Donnerstag, den 16. November - Reuters (German)

{{20171116T054834.229+0000}}Guten Morgen von Reuters am Donnerstag, den 16. NovemberTOP NEWS:

* JAMAIKA: Vor dem geplanten Ende der Sondierungen einer Jamaika-Koalition trennen CDU, CSU,
FDP und Grüne nach wie vor massive Meinungsverschiedenheiten. "Da muss morgen schon ein
ziemlicher Sprung nach vorne kommen", sagte CSU-Generalsekretär Scheuer nach stundenlangen
Beratungen der Unterhändler in immer wieder unterschiedlichen Zusammensetzungen. Auch
Grünen-Politikerin Roth sah noch "richtig, richtig viele Baustellen". CDU-Präsidiumsmitglied
Spahn sagte der "Passauer Neuen Presse", es werde keine Koalition um jeden Preis geben. Derweil
pocht die FDP auf den Abbau des Solidaritätszuschlages.

* SIEMENS will die Belegschaft über die Pläne für einen massiven Stellenabbau in
der Kraftwerks-Sparte informieren. Am Vormittag tritt der Wirtschaftsausschuss zusammen, um über
die Zukunft der Produktion von Turbinen für Gas- und Dampfkraftwerke zu beraten. Dort droht
angesichts der Energiewende in den nächsten Jahren ein weltweiter Auftragsschwund, der ganze
Werke überflüssig machen könnte. Bis zu 4000 der rund 8000 Arbeitsplätze in der
Turbinen-Produktion in Deutschland stehen zur Disposition. Der Industriekonzern hat
betriebsbedingte Kündigungen nicht ausgeschlossen.

What to Watch in the Day Ahead - Thursday, November 16 - 路透新闻

{{20171115T193111.136+0000}}What to Watch in the Day Ahead - Thursday, November 16(The Day Ahead is an email and PDF publication that includes the day's major stories and events, analyses and other features. To receive The Day Ahead, Eikon users can register at [DAY/US]. Thomson One users can register at RT/DAY/US. All times in ET/GMT)

Wal-Mart Stores Inc is expected to report a thirteenth straight quarter of comparable sales growth driven by an increase in customer traffic at its stores. Gross margins are likely to contract as the world's largest retailer continues to invest heavily in cutting prices and pours more money into its online business. Investors will be keen to hear what the management has to stay about traffic trends during the holiday seasons as well as whether the company's pricing initiatives have helped it gain market share amid price wars in the U.S. grocery industry. Industrial production data for October is due and is predicted to have risen 0.5 percent, compared to a 0.3 percent increase in September. (0830/1330) Meanwhile, both import prices and export prices in October likely rose 0.4 percent. (0830/1330) Weekly initial jobless claims data is expected to show a drop to 235,000 in the week ended Nov. 11 from 239,000 in the previous week. (0830/1330) The Philly Fed Business Indexes for November are also due. (0830/1330) All eyes will be on the electronics retailer Best Buy Co Inc's fourth-quarter forecast with the holiday months historically making up nearly half of the company's profit. Third-quarter profit is expected to rise with company's ongoing cost-cutting initiatives while comparable-store sales may be hurt by hurricanes. Cleveland Federal Reserve Chief Loretta Mester is scheduled to speak before the Cato Institute 35th Annual Monetary Conference in Washington. (0910/1410) Fed President Robert Kaplan participates in a moderated Q&A session before the CFA Society Houston. (1310/1810) Federal Reserve Board Governor Lael Brainard speaks on "Fintech" before the Third Annual Financial Stability Conference hosted by the U.S. Treasury Department Office of Financial Research and the University of Michigan Center on Finance, Law, and Policy, in Ann Arbor. (1545/2045) San Francisco Federal Reserve Bank President John Williams speaks at the San Francisco Fed's Asia Economic Policy Conference. (1630/2130) Chip equipment maker Applied Materials Inc is expected to report a rise in quarterly net sales and income helped by strong demand from smartphone makers, coupled with strength in its display business. Investors and analysts will be on the lookout for company's fiscal 2018 first-quarter forecast. Viacom Inc, the owner of MTV, Comedy Central, reports fourth-quarter earnings. The company's domestic affiliate revenue, the fees it collects from cable TV operators as well as online distributors, is expected to dip. In October, Viacom and Charter Communications agreed to a distribution deal that puts eight of Viacom's most popular networks in Charter's cheapest U.S. cable bundle, a source told Reuters. Investors and analysts will be looking for confirmation on that and news on other possible deals. AT&T CFO John Stephens will speak at a Morgan Stanley conference in Europe. The company's CEO Randall Stephenson said last week AT&T was ready to litigate as it pursues approval from the Justice Department for its proposed acquisition of Time Warner for $85.4 billion. Liberty Media Chairman John Malone and President Greg Maffei talk about their portfolio of media companies and telecom providers at the company's investor day. Bank of England Governor Mark Carney, Deputy Governor for Monetary Policy Ben Broadbent, Deputy Governor for Financial Stability Jon Cunliffe, Chief Cashier Jo Place, Deputy Governors Dave Ramsden and Sam Woods participate in Future Forum, St George's Hall Liverpool. (0900/1400) J M Smucker Co, which reports second-quarter earnings, trimmed its full-year earnings forecast in August, citing weak demand for coffee as retailers placed fewer orders due to the rising cost of coffee. The Folgers coffee maker lowered prices in response, which hit margins, but said it expects better margins further into the year. Gap Inc reports third-quarter results. The clothing retailer's earnings are expected to have benefited from a boost in demand for its lower-end Old Navy apparel and activewear brand Athleta. Chinese financial planning platform Jianpu Technology Inc, a unit of fintech firm Rong360, intends to debut its American Depository shares on the New York Stock Exchange under the symbol "JT". The IPO represents the latest in a recent flurry of New York listings by Asian companies, joining other Chinese firms as well as startups from Singapore and Taiwan in tapping U.S. equity markets for capital this year. Canada's manufacturing sales are forecast to have declined by 0.3 percent in September, in line with slower economic growth in the second half of the year after a strong first six months. (0830/1330) ADP launches a new Canadian job market report with the release of payroll figures for October, the first report to potentially rival the official labor force survey released by Statistics Canada. While ADP's similar U.S. report is closely watched by markets, its track record predicting non-farm payrolls is spotty, and traders could view the Canadian figures with a grain of salt. The Bank of Canada releases its semi-annual publication of feature articles, which will include research on the neutral rate of interest and the factors behind the 2014 oil price decline. (1030/1530) LIVECHAT - OIL OUTLOOK Reuters correspondents Amanda Cooper and Jessica Resnick-Ault take your questions about energy markets in the rapid-fire, weekly segment "Lock, Stock and Barrel". (0930/1430) To join the conversation, click here http://tmsnrt.rs/2lExMPr

(Compiled by Benny Thomas in Bengaluru; Edited by Shounak Dasgupta) ((Benny.Thomas@thomsonreuters.com;))

BUZZ-PREVIEW: Wal-Mart earnings eyed after Target tumble - Reuters News

{{20171115T182356.008+0000}}BUZZ-PREVIEW: Wal-Mart earnings eyed after Target tumble** Wal-Mart Stores shares down 0.5 pct at $90.60 on Weds; Q3 results expected before the market open on Thurs

** Q3 estimate is for adj EPS of 97 cents on revenue of $120.997 bln

** Retailer has topped EPS estimates for at least eight straight qtrs; Q2 revenue beat expectations to snap a three qtr losing streak

** Shares of rival Target tumbled 8.4 pct at $55.02 on Weds after its holiday-qtr profit forecast fell short of analyst expectations [nL3N1NL45J]

** WMT total same store sales for Q3 expected to rise 1.8 pct, according to Thomson Reuters data; estimates range from 1.4 pct to 2 pct

** Current mean recommendation of 32 analysts is "buy"; median price target of $91 is up from $84 three months ago

** WMT options imply a 3.4 pct swing in either direction by Fri, slightly less than the stock's 3.6 pct avg one-day move after earnings, over the last 8 qtrs, per Trade Alert data

UPDATE 2-Amazon cuts prices again at Whole Foods ahead of the holidays - Reuters News

{{20171115T172129.914+0000}}UPDATE 2-Amazon cuts prices again at Whole Foods ahead of the holidays(Adds graphic, analysts' comments, Whole Food spokeswoman, share prices and background)

By Sruthi Ramakrishnan

Nov 15 (Reuters) - Amazon.com Inc said on Wednesday it will offer more discounts and steeper price cuts at Whole Foods Market on many organic foods and groceries popular during the holidays.

The plan was announced just ahead of Thanksgiving and is on the heels of price cuts in August when Amazon completed its $13.7 billion acquisition of Whole Foods. [nL2N1LE12C]

"Price cuts are permanent," Brooke Buchanan, a spokeswoman for Whole Foods, told Reuters in an email.

Investors have been closely watching for price cuts at Whole Foods, concerned that cheaper prices would further hurt U.S. grocers already struggling to stay competitive with Amazon and Wal-Mart Stores Inc , which are locked in an intense battle for market share.

"Ever since Amazon bought Whole Foods Market, this is exactly what the other grocery store competitors have been fearing," Fort Pitt Capital analyst Kim Forrest told Reuters.

"Other grocers are going to have to come back in competitive replies – and it could be better service, better products and better pricing."

Shares of rival U.S. grocers Costco , Sprouts Farmers Market and Kroger all fell on Wednesday morning between 1 percent to 2 percent after the news. Target Corp's stock also moved lower. The shares were already pressured after the company forecasted disappointing earnings for the key holiday quarter. [nL3N1NL45J]

Amazon, which forayed into brick-and-mortar retailing with Whole Foods, could upend the grocery industry with its deep pockets and large presence, analysts have said.

In September, Target slashed prices on thousands of items, including cereal and baby formula, and said it would continue to offer discounts on some products in addition to the price-cuts. (http://bit.ly/2vT4elO)

Prices at Whole Foods, however, are still higher than most grocery stores because it caters to an up-market clientele.

"As we saw with Sprouts Farmer and really other grocery reports, the prior cuts haven't had a material impact on leading players," said Oppenheimer analyst Rupesh Parikh.

"(Whole Food) prices are still quite high versus peers," he said.

Sprouts Farmer reported better-than-expected third-quarter profit and net sales this month and raised its full-year forecasts. [nL4N1N857G]

Amazon said on Wednesday that Whole Foods will sell organic turkeys for $3.49 per pound to all customers, while Amazon Prime members can buy them at $2.99 a pound. [nBw2yqGLca]

The company said it will also offer lower prices on items from national brands including Chobani Yogurt and Applegate Hot Dogs, as well as smaller organic brands such as Eden Foods.

A study last month showed Whole Foods' previous price cuts on items including bananas, avocados and beef had drawn customers away from Wal-Mart, Trader Joe's and Sprouts Farmers. [nL2N1ME0RO]

<^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^ U.S. grocer stocks after Amazon buys Whole Foods http://reut.rs/2A0jij8

^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^> (Reporting by Sruthi Ramakrishnan in Bengaluru; Additional reporting by Rama Venkat Raman and Karina D'souza; Editing by Sayantani Ghosh and Bernard Orr) ((sruthi.ramakrishnan@thomsonreuters.com ; Within U.S. +1 646 223 8780, outside U.S. +91 80 6749 1130; Reuters Messaging: sruthi.ramakrishnan.thomsonreuters.com@reuters.net;))

Guten Abend von Reuters am Mittwoch, den 15. November - Reuters (German)

{{20171115T170629.244+0000}}Guten Abend von Reuters am Mittwoch, den 15. NovemberTOP NEWS:

* JAMAIKA: Im Countdown bei den Jamaika-Sondierungen haben CDU, CSU, FDP und Grüne am
Mittwoch in verschiedenen Themenfeldern weitere Schritte aufeinander zu gemacht, in zentralen
Fragestellungen etwa der Europa- und Flüchtlingspolitik aber noch keine Einigung erzielen
können. "Es wird immer klarer: Jamaika wird keine Lustreise, sondern ein hartes Experiment. Und
einige Expeditionsteilnehmer haben den Kompass noch nicht richtig eingestellt", sagte
CSU-Generalsekretär Scheuer. Beim Streitthema Migration kamen sich die Unterhändler unter
anderem bei der Fachkräftezuwanderung näher. Die Frage nach der insbesondere von der Union
geforderten Belastungsgrenze oder zum Familiennachzug blieben jedoch offen. Auch die
Verhandlungen zu Europa wurden ohne wirkliche Fortschritte vertagt.

* VOLKSWAGEN wird die Fahnder nicht los. Gerade erst sind die EU-Ermittler
abgezogen, die mutmaßlichen Kartellabsprachen nachgehen, da bekommt der Wolfsburger Konzern
schon wieder Besuch. Staatsanwälte und Steuerfahnder durchsuchten am Dienstag die Büros von
Finanzvorstand Witter, Personalvorstand Blessing und Betriebsratschef Osterloh, wie VW
einräumte. Hintergrund sind angeblich überhöhte Zahlungen an den Betriebsratsvorsitzenden, der
bei Volkswagen eine besondere Macht hat. VW und die Arbeitnehmervertretung wiesen diesen
Verdacht am Mittwoch zurück. Die jüngste Razzia ist ein weiterer Rückschlag für den Konzern, der
wegen "Dieselgate" ohnehin in einer Glaubwürdigkeitskrise steckt.

* DEUTSCHE BANK: Der US-Finanzinvestor Cerberus[CBS.UL] setzt seine Einkaufstour
in Deutschland fort und beteiligt sich nach der Commerzbank nun auch am Flaggschiff
Deutsche Bank. Die Amerikaner sicherten sich einen Anteil von drei Prozent an Deutschland
größtem Geldhaus im Wert von fast einer Milliarde Euro, wie aus einer Stimmrechtsmitteilung
hervorgeht. Damit steigt Cerberus zum viertgrößten Aktionär auf - nach dem chinesischen Konzern
HNA, dem Emirat Katar und dem weltgrößten Vermögensverwalter Blackrock. An der Commerzbank - die
immer wieder als langfristiger Fusionspartner der Deutschen Bank gehandelt wird - hält der
Investor seit dem Sommer fünf Prozent.

* SIEMENS will die Belegschaft am Donnerstag über die Pläne für einen massiven
Stellenabbau in der Kraftwerks-Sparte informieren. Am Vormittag tritt der Wirtschaftsausschuss
zusammen, um über die Zukunft der Produktion von Turbinen für Gas- und Dampfkraftwerke zu
beraten. Dort droht angesichts der Energiewende in den nächsten Jahren ein weltweiter
Auftragsschwund, der ganze Werke überflüssig machen könnte. Bis zu 4000 der rund 8000
Arbeitsplätze in der Turbinen-Produktion in Deutschland stehen zur Disposition. Der
Industriekonzern hat betriebsbedingte Kündigungen nicht ausgeschlossen.

* MÄRKTE: Europas Aktienanleger haben einige Gewinne der vergangenen Wochen eingestrichen.
Allerdings machten im Tagesverlauf Fusionsspekulationen im deutschen Bankensektor den Investoren
wieder Kauflaune. Somit schloss der Dax<.GDAXI> mit 12.976 Punkten nur noch 0,4 Prozent
niedriger. Er war zeitweise um 1,4 Prozent bis auf 12.847 Punkte gefallen. Der
EuroStoxx50<.STOXX50E> schloss 0,3 Prozent schwächer. An der Wall Street lagen zum
Handelsschluss in Europa der Dow Jones<.DJI>, der S&P500<.SPX> und der Nasdaq<.IXIC> je etwas
weniger als ein halbes Prozent im Minus.

* DEUTSCHE BÖRSE : HypoVereinsbank-Chef Theodor Weimer darf sich einem
Insider zufolge Hoffnungen auf den bald vakanten Chefposten bei der Deutschen Börse
machen. Der 57-jährige Weimer sei ein aussichtsreicher Kandidat für die Nachfolge von Kengeter,
der über den Vorwurf des Insiderhandels gestolpert war, sagte eine mit der Suche vertraute
Person am Mittwoch der Nachrichtenagentur Reuters. In Unternehmenskreisen der Börse hieß es,
Weimers Profil würde zu den Anforderungen passen, die Aufsichtsratschef Faber an den neuen Mann
habe.

* PROSIEBENSAT.1-Chef Ebeling sorgt mit abschätzigen Äußerungen über
Fernsehzuschauer für Aufregung. "Es gibt Menschen, die ein bisschen fettleibig sind und ein
bisschen arm, die immer noch gerne auf der Couch sitzen, sich zurücklehnen und wirklich gerne
unterhalten werden", sagte der Vorstandschef der Senderkette aus ProSieben, Sat.1, Kabel 1 und
mehreren Spartensendern in einer Analystenkonferenz vor einer Woche. "Das ist eine wichtige
Zuschauergruppe, die sich nicht ändert."

FIRMEN UND BRANCHEN - WEITERE NACHRICHTEN UND TERMINE:

* SOFTBANK<9984.T> :Der japanische Mobilfunkkonzern will einem Medienbericht zufolge in den
kommenden drei bis vier Jahren insgesamt 25 Milliarden Dollar in Saudi-Arabien investieren. Wie
die Finanznachrichtenagentur Bloomberg am Mittwoch berichtete, will sich das Unternehmen allein
mit 15 Milliarden Dollar an der geplanten Retortenstadt Neom an der Grenze zu Jordanien und
Ägypten beteiligen. Zudem wolle der SoftBank-Fonds Vision Fund zehn Milliarden Dollar in den
staatlichen Energieversorger Saudi Electricity<5110.SE> stecken.

* IG METALL: In der ersten Tarifrunde der Metall- und Elektroindustrie ist der Streit über
die Arbeitszeit voll entbrannt. Die Arbeitgeberverbände in Niedersachsen, Berlin-Brandenburg und
Hamburg konfrontierten die Gewerkschaft IG Metall mit abgestimmten Forderungen nach höheren
Arbeitszeiten, weniger Überstundenzuschlägen und längerer Befristung. "Die Unternehmen brauchen
die Möglichkeit, individuell mit jedem Arbeitnehmer eine längere Arbeitszeit zu vereinbaren",
erklärte Moschko, Verhandlungsführer des Verbandes von Berlin-Brandenburg. Die IG Metall
gefährde mit ihrer Forderung nach einer Entgelterhöhung um sechs Prozent und einem Recht
einzelner auf Arbeitszeitverkürzung die Wettbewerbsfähigkeit der Firmen.

BLICKPUNKT ZENTRALBANKEN UND KONJUNKTUR:

* EU: Das Europäische Parlament hat mit großer Mehrheit ein neues Gesetz zum Schutz der
heimischen Industrie vor Billigimporten angenommen. Das neue Regelwerk wurde am Mittwoch mit 554
zu 48 Stimmen verabschiedet. Es stärkt die Abwehrmöglichkeiten der EU gegen subventionierte
Billigimporte aus Drittstaaten. Beispielsweise kann die EU bei der Erhebung von Zöllen die
Einhaltung von Umwelt- und Arbeitsschutzstandards in Betracht ziehen. Die Verschärfung sollen
bis Ende des Jahres in Kraft treten und dürften vor allem China treffen.

* USA: Die Inflation in den USA zieht leicht an und gibt Befürwortern einer baldigen
Zinserhöhung weitere Argumente an die Hand. Die US-Währungshüter achten besonders auf die
Preisveränderungen bei persönlichen Verbraucherausgaben (PCE), wobei Energie- und
Nahrungsmittelkosten außen vor bleiben. Hier gab es im Oktober einen geringfügigen Anstieg auf
1,8 Prozent. Damit näherte sich die Kenngröße dem Zielwert der Notenbank (Fed) von zwei Prozent
an.

BLICKPUNKT POLITIK:

* USA/STEUERREFORM: Die Republikaner im US-Senat stricken trotz zunehmenden Zeitdrucks
weiter an einer eigenen Gesetzesvorlage für die von Präsident Trump versprochene Steuerreform.
Der Finanzausschuss-Vorsitzende der Kongresskammer, Hatch, schlug umfangreiche Änderungen vor.
Unter anderem will er das Vorhaben mit der Rücknahme von Teilen der unter Trumps Vorgänger Obama
verabschiedeten Gesundheitsreform verknüpfen. Ob das eine Mehrheit mittragen würde, ist
fraglich, denn ungeachtet ihrer Kritik an ObamaCare sind sich die Republikaner bei dem Thema
uneins. Trotz ihrer Überzahl im Kongress und dem Druck des Präsidenten sind ihre Versuche zum
Rückbau der Gesundheitsreform bislang gescheitert.

* JAMAIKA: Die GRÜNEN sehen trotz weiter bestehender großer Meinungsverschiedenheiten
Fortschritte bei den Sondierungen für eine Jamaika-Koalition mit CDU, CSU und FDP, wie der
Unterhändler Jürgen Trittin der Nachrichtenagentur Reuters.

* GRÜNE/KLIMA/KOHLE: Die deutschen Kraftwerksbetreiber können nach den Worten der
Grünen-Chefin Peter nicht mit Entschädigungen für die Abschaltung von Kohlekraftwerken rechnen.
"Wir werden sicher nicht zustimmen, dass man die Stilllegung von Kohlekraftwerken durch
Entschädigungen vergoldet", sagte Peter der "Mitteldeutschen Zeitung". Das sei für die Grünen
vollkommen abwegig: "Wir wollen einen entschädigungsfreien Ausstieg."

* FRANKREICH/MACRON/KLIMA: Anders als Deutschland will das auf Atomkraft setzende Frankreich
nach Angaben von Präsident Macron in wenigen Jahren komplett auf Kohle-Energie verzichten.
Frankreich habe beschlossen, bis Ende 2021 alle Kohlekraftwerke stillzulegen, sagte Macron auf
der Weltklimakonferenz. Zudem wolle sein Land Erneuerbare Energien stärker fördern.

UPDATE 4-Target signals another weak holiday quarter, shares tumble  - Reuters News

{{20171115T165550.217+0000}}UPDATE 4-Target signals another weak holiday quarter, shares tumble (Adds new analyst comment, background on fourth-quarter performance)

By Richa Naidu and Sruthi Ramakrishnan

Nov 15 (Reuters) - Target Corp's holiday-quarter profit forecast fell short of analyst expectations, sending its shares down 10 percent on Wednesday as hopes faded that the retailer would make a shopping season comeback.

Target has missed Wall Street's fourth-quarter profit expectations for the past two years. It is gearing up for the holidays by cutting prices and introducing delivery options to compete with Wal-Mart Stores Inc and online sellers, moves that can lure customers but crimp margins.

"It was always unrealistic that Target was going to have a great holiday season in terms of sales or profitability," said Neil Saunders, managing director of GlobalData Retail, noting pressured margins were already expected based on company guidance.

"This is still a very competitive environment, and Target has no choice but to respond to that.. the problem is that Wall Street don't necessarily understand this," he added.

The big-box chain forecast adjusted earnings of $1.05 to $1.25 per share for the fourth quarter, a range largely below the average analyst estimate of $1.24. It expects same-store sales in the quarter in a range of flat to 2 percent higher.

The holiday season can represent 20 percent to 40 percent of annual sales for many retailers.

In October, Target said most of its holiday gifts would cost less than $15 and that it would offer customers free shipping beginning in November.

It also has hired 100,000 temporary holiday workers, up from 70,000 in each of the prior four years, and raised its minimum hourly wage this year by 10 percent.

Target shares have lost about 17 percent since the start of the year and were down 9.2 percent at $54.59 in midday trading.

Target's third-quarter gross margin slipped to 29.7 percent from 29.8 percent, and Chief Financial Officer Cathy Smith said margin pressure should continue into the holiday quarter.

Target will try to grab more of the lucrative holiday toy market, following the September bankruptcy and ongoing restructuring of Toys "R" Us, the biggest U.S. toy chain.

"We are playing to win in toys. We think there is opportunity to expand share," Chief Executive Brian Cornell said on a media call.

Third-quarter same-store sales topped estimates, rising 0.9 percent in the quarter as price cuts drove a 24 percent jump in comparable online sales. Analysts expected a 0.4 percent increase, according to Thomson Reuters I/B/E/S.

In a turnaround announced in February, Cornell vowed to double the number of small-format stores, invest heavily in e-commerce, aggressively promote products and keep grocery prices low to compete with Wal-Mart, Amazon.com Inc and supermarket chain Kroger Co . [nL3N1GD458]

Target's Chief Merchandising Officer Mark Tritton said comparable grocery sales rose slightly, helped by demand for produce.

But pricing pressure on groceries is continuing to intensify. Amazon on Wednesday unveiled more discounts on several products at its Whole Foods Market with Thanksgiving around the corner, sending shares in U.S. grocers lower. [nL3N1NL4S6]

Excluding items, Target earned a profit of 91 cents per share in the quarter ended Oct. 28, beating the average estimate of 86 cents. Sales rose 1.4 percent to $16.67 billion, topping the average estimate of $16.61 billion.

UPDATE 3-Loblaw ties up with Instacart to launch home deliveries  - Reuters News

{{20171115T164044.100+0000}}UPDATE 3-Loblaw ties up with Instacart to launch home deliveries (Adds Instacart tie-up details, comments from company)

By Taenaz Shakir

Nov 15 (Reuters) - Canadian grocery and pharmacy chain Loblaw Cos Ltd said on Wednesday it is tying up with San Francisco-based Instacart to offer home delivery service in Toronto and Vancouver, as it tries to carve out more market share in a brutal retail sector.

The company will deliver food and other pantry staples from Loblaw's Real Canadian Superstore and T&T supermarkets to customers in Toronto starting Dec. 6, and in Vancouver starting in January, Loblaw Chief Executive Officer Galen Weston said on a conference call with analysts.

Home delivery startup Instacart counts Whole Foods , Costco , Target and more than 100 other retailers as customers for grocery deliveries. Instacart charges a delivery fee to bring items to customers.

Like many other Canadian retailers, Loblaw has lost market share to bigger American rivals, and it will also face cost pressure next year from rising minimum wages in its home province of Ontario. [nL1N1IW0X8]

Amazon's recent purchase of Whole Foods - which included Canadian locations - has put retailers against the wall. They have had to revamp their online and delivery services, as well as keep pricing competitive.

Loblaw's Weston said he still expects "2018 will be a very difficult year."

Earlier on Wednesday, Loblaw, which also operates Shoppers Drug Mart, said it would shut 22 unprofitable stores.

The company beat analysts' expectations for third-quarter profit and revenue thanks largely to a rise in same-store sales at its Shoppers Drug Mart outlets, which rose 3.3 percent in the quarter, up from 2.8 percent growth a year ago.

Same-store sales growth at its Loblaw groceries was flat at 1.4 percent in the quarter ended Oct. 7, compared with the year-earlier period.

Loblaw said the store closures would come across its brands and formats and would largely be completed by the end of the first quarter of 2018.

It had earlier said it would cut 500 jobs, planning to reinvest the savings in its digital and e-commerce businesses.

The Brampton, Ontario-based retailer expects to record charges for the layoffs and store closures of about C$135 million, most of which will be factored into the fourth quarter.

It expects annualized savings of about C$85 million from the changes.

Excluding items, the company earned C$1.39 per share, beating analysts' average estimate of C$1.30 per share, according to Thomson Reuters I/B/E/S.

Revenue was flat at C$14.19 billion, but beat analysts' estimate of C$14.10 billion.

Loblaw shares were up 2 percent at C$70.39 Wednesday morning on the Toronto Stock Exchange.

($1 = 1.2742 Canadian dollars)

(Reporting by Taenaz Shakir, additional reporting by Nishara Karuvalli Pathikkal in Bengaluru; Editing by Patrick Graham and Bernard Orr) ((Nishara.KaruvalliPathikkal@thomsonreuters.com; within U.S. +1 646 223 8780, outside U.S. +91 80 6749 6633; Reuters Messaging: Nishara.karuvallipathikkal.thomsonreuters.com@reuters.net))

Whole Foods (Amazon) baisse ses prix avant Thanksgiving - Reuters (French)

{{20171115T150552.994+0000}}Whole Foods (Amazon) baisse ses prix avant Thanksgiving15 novembre (Reuters) - Whole Foods Market, la chaîne de supermarchés bio acquise cet été par Amazon.com , a annoncé mercredi des baisses de prix pour ses produits les plus vendus et des articles de saison à l'approche de la période des fêtes, faisant baisser ses concurrents à Wall Street dans la crainte d'une guerre des prix.

Ces mesures, accompagnées d'offres promotionnelles supplémentaires pour les abonnés d'Amazon Prime, viennent s'ajouter aux baisses de prix déjà annoncées par Whole Foods en août, après la finalisation de son rachat pour 13,7 milliards de dollars (11,6 milliards de dollars) par le géant américain du commerce en ligne.

L'annonce fait baisser les distributeurs rivaux Wal-Mart , Kroger et Costco dans les premiers échanges à Wall Street. Le secteur des biens de consommation essentiels recule de 0,69% <.SPLRCS>.

Les investisseurs scrutent de près tout signe de valse des étiquettes chez Whole Foods, qui n'a jamais été réputé pour ses prix bas, de crainte d'une nouvelle guerre des prix dans un secteur déjà mis à mal par une rude concurrence.

A l'approche de Thanksgiving, Whole Foods propose des dindes biologiques à 3,49 dollars la livre, et même 2,99 dollars pour les abonnés d'Amazon Prime.

La chaîne baisse aussi les prix de marques nationales comme les yoghourts Chobani ou les hot dogs Applegate. La marque de produits bio Eden Foods est également concernée.

"Ce sont les derniers en date de nos prix plus bas dans le cadre de notre intégration au sein d'Amazon", a déclaré dans un communiqué le directeur général de Whole Foods, John Mackey.

Une étude a montré le mois dernier que les précédentes baisses de prix de Whole Foods, notamment sur les bananes, les avocats et le boeuf, avaient attiré dans ses rayons des clients jusque-là fidèles à Wal-Mart , Trader Joe's et Sprouts Farmers.

Whole Foods est la première incursion d'Amazon dans la distribution alimentaire physique.

(Sruthi Ramakrishnan à Bangalore, Véronique Tison pour le service français) (((Service économique); (tél 01 49 49 53 87);))Copyright (c) 2017 Thomson Reuters

POINT MARCHÉS-Wall Street recule, plombée par la baisse du pétrole - Reuters (French)

{{20171115T150541.450+0000}}POINT MARCHÉS-Wall Street recule, plombée par la baisse du pétrole15 novembre (Reuters) - La Bourse de New York poursuit son repli en début de séance mercredi, pénalisée la baisse par les cours du pétrole et le recul de plusieurs grands distributeurs face à une nouvelle offensive d'Amazon sur les prix.

L'indice Dow Jones <.DJI> perd 161,05 points, soit 0,69%, à 23.248,42. Le Standard & Poor's 500 <.SPX>, plus large, recule de 0,75% à 2.559,55 et le Nasdaq Composite <.IXIC> cède 0,87% à 6.679,48.

L'indice de volatilité du CBOE <.VIX> est en hausse de plus de deux points, au plus haut depuis le 21 août.

Les prix du baril de Brent et du brut léger américain (West Texas Intermediate, WTI) poursuivent leur repli et perdent plus de 1% après l'abaissement par l'Agence internationale de l'Energie (AIE) de sa prévision de demande mondiale pour cette année et pour 2018, qui s'est ajouté à une série d'indicateurs chinois moins bons que prévu. .

L'annonce par l'association professionnelle API d'une hausse inattendue des stocks de brut aux Etats-Unis a encore accru la pression sur les cours de l'or noir. [nL8N1NK3LR] Dans ce contexte, les investisseurs suivront avec attention la publication à 15h30 GMT des données officielles sur les stocks américains.

En attendant, le compartiment lié à l'énergie <.SPNY> baisse de 1,47% et celui des matières premières <.SPLRCM> de 1%.

Les titres Exxon et Chevron perdent respectivement 1,01% et 0,5%.

Sur le marché des changes, le dollar a momentanément accentué ses pertes après la publication, une heure avant l'ouverture des marchés actions, d'une série d'indicateurs macroéconomiques.

Les prix à la consommation ont très légèrement augmenté le mois dernier malgré la dissipation des effets de l'ouragan Harvey sur le prix de l'essence, tandis que la hausse des loyers et des tarifs dans le secteur de la santé suggère un renforcement progressif de l'inflation sous-jacente. [nL8N1NL55Q]

TARGET CHUTE, SES PRÉVISIONS DÉÇOIVENT

Les ventes au détail ont parallèlement enregistré une croissance inattendue en octobre grâce à une hausse des achats automobiles, qui ont compensé la baisse de la demande de matériaux de construction. [nL8N1NL5CO]

Enfin, l'enquête mensuelle "Empire State" de la Réserve fédérale de New York a montré un ralentissement plus important que prévu ces dernières semaines de l'activité manufacturière dans la région après son rebond du mois d'octobre. [nL8N1NL5A6]

Le billet vert est revenu à son plus bas niveau depuis un mois face à un panier de devises de référence après ces statistiques, avant d'effacer une partie de ses pertes, limitant ainsi son repli à 0,18% <.DXY>.

Le rendement des Treasuries à 10 ans recule lui aussi, à 2,329%.

Les valeurs de la distribution et plusieurs grands groupes alimentaires chutent par ailleurs après l'annonce par Amazon et sa filiale Whole Foods de baisses de prix pour la période des fêtes.

Wal-Mart cède 0,49%, Costco 0,66% et Kroger 1,95%. Le secteur des biens de consommations recule de 0,67% <.SPLRCS>.

Toujours dans la distribution, Target chute de 8,39% après l'annonce d'une prévision de bénéfice ajusté pour la période des fêtes inférieure aux attentes des analystes.

Le titre Snap cède 0,8% à la suite de l'annonce de la liquidation de la participation du fonds de l'investisseur américain George Soros.

En Europe, les places financières évoluent dans le rouge. Le CAC 40 <.FCHI> perd 0,73% et le Stoxx 600 <.STOXX> 0,91%.

USA-Les valeurs à suivre à Wall Street (actualisé) - Reuters (French)

{{20171115T140600.970+0000}}USA-Les valeurs à suivre à Wall Street (actualisé)(Actualisé avec valeurs de la distribution et Conagra, Acorda Therapeutics, cours en avant-Bourse)

15 novembre (Reuters) - Principales valeurs à suivre mercredi à Wall Street, où les contrats à terme sur les indices de référence signalent une ouverture en baisse de 0,4% à 0,5% :

* Plusieurs valeurs de la grande distribution baissent en avant-Bourse après l'annonce par AMAZON et sa filiale Whole Foods Market de baisses de prix pendant la période des fêtes. COSTCO cède 1,2%, KROGER 1,5%, WAL-MART STORES 0,6%. Egalement affecté, le grossiste alimentaire CONAGRA BRANDS chute de 7,3%.

* TARGET a fait état mercredi d'une hausse de 0,9%, meilleure qu'attendu, de ses ventes à magasins comparables sur le trimestre clos fin octobre, mais sa prévision de bénéfice ajusté pour la période des fêtes est inférieure au consensus. Le titre cède 4,3% en avant-Bourse.

* ALPHABET - La maison mère de Google, sera visée par d'autres affaires, a déclaré mercredi la commissaire européenne à la concurrence, Margrethe Vestager, lors d'un voyage à Pékin. [nL8N1NL3HN]

* APPLE - Le taïwanais Foxconn <2317.TW>, qui fabrique l'iPhone X pour Apple, a annoncé une chute de 39% de son bénéfice au troisième trimestre, un résultat nettement plus faible que prévu, le premier sous-traitant mondial en électronique ayant vu baisser ses marges du fait de goulets d'étranglement dans la production du nouveau smartphone du géant américain. Apple perd 0,5% en avant-Bourse. [nL8N1NL18S]

* AMAZON perd 0,5% en avant-Bourse. Selon des sources approchées par Reuters, le géant du commerce en ligne renonce à son projet de lancer un service de vidéo en ligne associant des programmes de diffuseurs et de réseaux câblés.

* EXXON et CHEVRON perdent chacun autour de 0,7% en avant-Bourse sur fond de chute des cours du brut dans le sillage de l'abaissement par l'Agence internationale de l'Energie (AIE) de sa prévision de demande mondiale pour cette année et 2018.

* IBM - Le titre a perd 0,8% en avant-Bourse au lendemain de l'annonce d'une nouvelle réduction de la participation de Berkshire Hathaway , l'entreprise de Warren Buffett, au capital du groupe informatique. [nL8N1NK9XI]

* BOEING - La compagnie à bas coûts de Dubaï Flydubai s'apprête à passer une commande de 175 Boeing 737 MAX, a-t-on appris de sources proches du dossier. [nL8N1NL1M5]

* SNAP perd 1,8% en avant-Bourse après l'annonce de la liquidation de la participation du fonds de l'investisseur américain George Soros. L'action Snap a plongé de 48,65% depuis sa première cotatiion en mars. JMP Securities a abaissé sa recommandation à "performance de marché" contre "surperformance".

* AIR PRODUCTS - Le spécialiste des gaz industriels a annoncé la prolongation jusqu'au 30 septembre 2022 du mandat de son PDG, Seifi Ghasemi.

* CARDINAL HEALTH - Shanghai Pharmaceuticals Holding <601607.SS> a annoncé l'acquisition de l'activité de distribution de médicaments en Chine de Cardinal Health pour 557 millions de dollars (475 millions d'euros).

* ACORDA THERAPEUTICS chute de près de 40% en avant-Bourse après l'annonce de l'arrêt du recrutement de deux essais cliniques de son traitement de la maladie de Parkinson tozadenant.

CORRECTED-Wal-Mart partners with Lord & Taylor to expand online fashion presence - Reuters News

{{20171114T164739.848+0000}}CORRECTED-Wal-Mart partners with Lord & Taylor to expand online fashion presence(In 7th paragraph, corrects to say that Wal-Mart is the largest clothing retailer in the United States, not the world)

By Nandita Bose

CHICAGO, Nov 13 (Reuters) - Wal-Mart Stores Inc said on Monday it will offer Hudson's Bay Co- owned department store chain Lord & Taylor dedicated space on its website, as it looks to make deeper inroads into the fast-growing online fashion business.

The world's largest retailer will start offering higher-end clothing and accessories from Lord & Taylor to its customers in spring 2018.

The partnership will allow Lord & Taylor to open a virtual storefront on Walmart.com and boost customer traffic to its website by reaching a wider audience. It will boost Wal-Mart's online assortment with premium products and advance the retailer's effort to access millennial customers who usually do not shop on Walmart.com.

"Our goal is to create a premium fashion destination within Walmart.com," Denise Incandela, Head of Fashion, Walmart U.S. eCommerce told Reuters in an interview on Monday. She said Wal-Mart shoppers search the retailer's website for premium items and the company aims to expand its online business with a focus on such products.

"This is a part of a larger business strategy where we are working to create a new Walmart.com," Incandela said. She did not comment on the financial terms of the partnership.

In the past year, Wal-Mart has been acquiring small online fashion brands like Shoebuy, Modcloth and Bonobos in an attempt to recover lost ground against Amazon and others in the online fashion world. Wal-Mart is the largest brick-and-mortar clothing retailer in the United State, with 2016 sales for that category exceeding $23 billion, according to retail think tank Fung Global Retail & Technology. But despite its store muscle, Wal-Mart has failed to replicate that success online. It has not only struggled to attract the type of affluent young consumers who tend to shop for clothes online but due to its low-income customer base and brand perception, has also faced challenges in persuading well-known apparel brands to sell on its website.

Amazon leads the U.S. online clothing and footwear market with sales of $13 billion in 2016, up $9 billion from five years ago. It is expected to triple its share of the U.S. apparel market over the next four years, according to data from Euromonitor and Forrester. Virtual storefronts have become a strong e-commerce tool with retailers including Amazon.com Inc and Alibaba Group Holding Ltd routinely offering dedicated space to brands on their website. Virtual stores are also a preferred route for U.S. retailers to enter new countries where they don't have operations. For example, Macy's in 2015 said it would enter China with a virtual store on Alibaba and test demand in that market.

(Reporting by Nandita Bose Editing by Sandra Maler) ((nandita.bose@thomsonreuters.com; +13124088726; Reuters Messaging: nandita.bose.reuters.com@reuters.net))

UPDATE 1-UK grocery inflation hits highest level in four years - Kantar Worldpanel - Reuters News

{{20171114T104955.648+0000}}UPDATE 1-UK grocery inflation hits highest level in four years - Kantar Worldpanel* Grocery inflation 3.4 pct in 12 weeks to Nov. 5

* UK grocery sales up 3.2 pct

* Sainsbury's best performer of big four UK grocers

(Adds detail,)

LONDON, Nov 14 (Reuters) - British grocery inflation hit its
highest level since November 2013 in the past quarter, driving
supermarkets' sales growth, industry data showed on Tuesday.

Market researcher Kantar Worldpanel said grocery inflation
was 3.4 percent in the 12 weeks to Nov. 5, with prices rising
fastest in products such as butter, fish and cola and falling in
only a few products, including crisps and fresh poultry.

It said that over the course of a year, this could add 143.7
pounds ($188.2) to a typical family's grocery bill.

Official data released on Tuesday showed overall British
consumer price inflation held at an annual rate of 3.0 percent
in October, its highest level in five-and-a-half years.
[nU8N13000D]

Kantar Worldpanel said overall UK grocery sales increased in
value by 3.2 percent year on year in the 12-week period.

"Volume sales have increased by less than 1 percent, meaning
it's price rises keeping supermarket performance buoyant,"
Fraser McKevitt, head of retail and consumer insight at Kantar
Worldpanel.

Of Britain's big four grocers, Sainsbury's , the No.
2 player, was the best performer for the first time since April
2016, with a sales rise of 2.6 percent.

Sales at market leader Tesco  increased 2.3 percent.
Morrisons  and Asda  followed with rises of 2.1
percent and 1.5 percent respectively.

However, all of the big four still lost market share to
German discounters Aldi and Lidl, which continue to open lots of
new space.

Lidl was Britain's fastest growing supermarket for the fifth
straight period with sales up 15.1 percent. Rival Aldi's sales
rose 13.1 percent.

 Sainsbury's      16.2          16.3          2.6

 Morrisons        10.4          10.5          2.1
 Aldi             6.7           6.1           13.1
 Co-Operative     6.1           6.4           -1.5
 Lidl             5.1           4.6           15.1
 Waitrose         5.3           5.3           2.3
 Iceland          2.0           2.1           1.1

Source: Kantar Worldpanel

UK grocery inflation hits highest level since 2013 - Kantar Worldpanel - Reuters News

{{20171114T082112.055+0000}}UK grocery inflation hits highest level since 2013 - Kantar WorldpanelLONDON, Nov 14 (Reuters) - British grocery inflation was 3.4 percent in the 12 weeks to Nov. 5, its highest level since November 2013, industry data showed on Tuesday.

Market researcher Kantar Worldpanel said prices are rising fastest in markets such as butter, fish and cola and are falling in only a few markets, including crisps and fresh poultry.

Kantar said overall UK grocery sales increased in value by 3.2 percent year on year in the 12 week period.

Of Britain's big four grocers, Sainsbury's , the No. 2 player, was the best performer with a sales rise of 2.6 percent, followed by market leader Tesco , with an increase of 2.3 percent. Asda and Morrisons followed with rises of 1.5 percent and 2.1 percent respectively.

Discounter Lidl was Britain's fastest growing supermarket for the fifth straight period with sales up 15.1 percent. Rival Aldi's sales rose 13.1 percent.

BREAKINGVIEWS-Hasbro Mattel bid would put Barbie in the corner - Reuters Breakingviews

{{20171113T152424.352+0000}}BREAKINGVIEWS-Hasbro Mattel bid would put Barbie in the corner(Refiles to correct Hasbro stock symbol in first paragraph. The author is a Reuters Breakingviews columnist. The opinions expressed are his own.)

By John Foley

LONDON, Nov 13 (Reuters Breakingviews) - To mangle a line from "Dirty Dancing", nobody puts Barbie in the corner. Except maybe Hasbro, which wants to acquire arch-rival toy maker Mattel , according to Reuters. That would bring together brands like Hasbro's Star Wars and Mattel's Fisher-Price, among many. The companies, with a combined value on Friday of $16 billion, have decades of enmity to overcome – but these days Barbie and American Girl on Mattel's side and Hasbro's Disney Princess crowd have more dangerous foes than each other.

Since Mattel made a hostile offer for Hasbro in 1996, a lot has changed. Mattel is now unambiguously the smaller and less profitable of the two. And the antitrust concerns that Hasbro used to rebuff Mattel seem almost quaint. The options for children's entertainment have exploded since the 1990s. It's hard to imagine a combined 50 percent share of the market for dolls – which has barely grown for the past decade, according to Jefferies – is that much of a threat to anyone.

The two companies operate differently, but that may mean there's scope for cost savings. Mattel, for instance, makes around half of its own toys, according to UBS. That saddles it with a workforce six times the size of Hasbro's, which outsources manufacturing. Mattel's American Girl has its own retail stores, too. The relatively asset-heavy strategy isn't working. Mattel's share price has halved in a year.

Boss Margo Giorgiadis, imported earlier this year from Google, has a plan to slash costs equivalent to 10 percent of the company's sales. Say Hasbro, which has much higher operating margins, can squeeze out half as much again, or an extra $250 million a year. Tax and capitalise that additional profit, and the roughly $3.4 billion in value creation easily covers a 30 percent premium to Mattel's $4.8 billion undisturbed stock-market value, with a little left over.

Feuds in the toybox are the big obstacle. Hasbro previously snatched brands like Sesame Street and Disney Princess from Mattel. Some franchises have gone the other way, too. The likes of Marvel and DC, which license Mattel to make toys using their characters, might squawk. Nonetheless, the bankruptcy of toy-store chain Toys R Us shows meaner enemies are close by. Faced with tech disruption and playground bullies like Amazon and Wal-Mart , childish squabbles are best left behind.

On Twitter https://twitter.com/johnsfoley

CONTEXT NEWS

- Hasbro has made an approach to acquire rival toymaker Mattel, Reuters reported on Nov. 10, citing sources familiar with the matter.

- Mattel had a market capitalisation of $5 billion at its closing share price on Nov. 10, roughly half what it was a year earlier. Hasbro's equity value was $11.4 billion, up nearly 10 percent.

- Mattel's brands include Barbie and Fisher-Price, while Hasbro makes Star Wars toys, Play-Doh and Monopoly. Hasbro also has the Disney Princess franchise, which it started developing in 2016 after winning a contract with Disney that ended a partnership with Mattel.

- The two companies have discussed merging on several occasions in the past. In 1996, Hasbro rejected an all-share offer from Mattel, saying it would fail for antitrust reasons.

- Mattel reported earnings of $0.09 per share adjusted for one-off factors on Oct. 26, missing analyst estimates of $0.56, and suspended its quarterly dividend.

BREAKINGVIEWS-China's JD-Alibaba rivalry enters new phase - Reuters Breakingviews

{{20171113T132540.455+0000}}BREAKINGVIEWS-China's JD-Alibaba rivalry enters new phase(The author is a Reuters Breakingviews columnist. The opinions expressed are her own.)

By Robyn Mak

HONG KONG, Nov 13 (Reuters Breakingviews) - China's fiercest e-commerce rivalry is entering a new, potentially volatile phase. A jump in third-quarter sales and a surprise net profit for the period show the $57 billion JD.com is reining in costs while keeping up with Alibaba , its much larger e-commerce rival. But Jack Ma's $477 billion behemoth is muscling in on key domains like logistics and food. That's a threat for JD's already thin margins.

Monday's results confirm China's second-largest e-commerce group, led by Richard Liu, is getting stronger. Revenue in the three months to September rose 39 percent to 84 billion yuan ($13 billion), the company said on Monday, thanks to an uptick in shoppers on its sites. JD, which holds inventory and invests heavily in its own logistics and delivery network much as Amazon.com does, also swung to an unexpected net profit in the quarter for only the second time since going public in May 2014. If things stay on track, JD should deliver its first annual profit next year.

Yet Alibaba looms large over JD's fortunes. The bigger company is moving on from its "asset-light" model, in which it provided online platforms for others to trade but did little of the real-world grunt-work. It is now pouring money into an effort to catch up with JD in logistics and delivery. This pits the two directly against each other in areas such as online groceries, where refrigerated warehouses and same-day delivery, for instance, are critical to winning market share. During the past weekend's so-called Singles Day shopping festival, for example, the two battled each other to deliver fresh hairy crabs and frozen Chilean salmon to bargain hunters across the country.

JD's early lead in logistics, as well as deep-pocketed backers like Tencent <0700.HK> and Wal-Mart , help position it to fend off Alibaba. But the leeway is already razor thin: in August, the company reckoned adjusted net margins for this year will be between 0.5 percent and 1.5 percent. Even tiny increases in costs or reductions in prices can wipe out its profit. As of Friday, shares of JD had fallen some 13 percent in three months but were still up more than 60 percent over a year. Investors will have to get used to the choppiness.

On Twitter https://twitter.com/mak_robyn

CONTEXT NEWS

- Chinese online retailer JD.com on Nov. 13 reported revenue of 83.7 billion yuan ($12.6 billion) in the three months to the end of September, an increase of 39 percent from the same period last year.

- The company reported a net profit attributable to ordinary shareholders of 1 billion yuan for the quarter, compared with a net loss of 467 million yuan from continuing operations a year earlier. Analysts polled by Thomson Reuters were expecting a mean net loss of 213 million yuan.

- On Nov. 12, JD.com announced that the value of all goods and services transacted on its shopping sites reached $19.1 billion during the Singles Day Shopping Festival, which ran from Nov. 1 to Nov. 11.

- Separately, Alibaba said transactions on its platforms topped $25.6 billion during one day, Nov. 11, also known as China's Singles Day. Alibaba's one-day sales figure was up 39 percent from a year earlier.

- JD.com ADRs were up around 6 percent at $42.50 at 6.03a.m. EST.

What to Watch in the Week Ahead and on Monday, November 13 - 路透新闻

{{20171110T193257.773+0000}}What to Watch in the Week Ahead and on Monday, November 13(The Day Ahead is an email and PDF publication that includes the day's major stories and events, analyses and other features. To receive The Day Ahead, Eikon users can register at [DAY/US]. Thomson One users can register at RT/DAY/US. All times in ET/GMT)

WEEKAHEAD

Federal Reserve Chair Janet Yellen participates in a policy panel before the 'European Central Bank Conference: Communications Challenges for Policy Effectiveness, Accountability and Reputation' in Frankfurt on Tuesday. ECB President Mario Draghi, Bank of Japan Governor Haruhiko Kuroda and Bank of England Governor Mark Carney also speak at the same conference. Chicago Federal Reserve President Charles Evans will also speak on the economy in a panel.

The world's largest retailer Wal-Mart Stores Inc is expected to report a thirteenth straight quarter of comparable sales growth on Thursday, driven by an increase in customer traffic at its stores. Gross margins are likely to contract as the retailer continues to invest heavily in cutting prices and pours more money into its online business.

Retail sales data for October on Wednesday and is likely to show a 0.1 percent rise. Producer price figures for October on Tuesday. Consumer Price Index numbers for October are expected the next day. On Friday, building permits figures for October are up for release and are likely to have edged higher to 1.24 million units. Industrial production data for October is due on Thursday and is expected to have risen 0.5 percent. The Philly Fed Business Indexes for November are also due on same day. NY Fed manufacturing figures for November is due on Wednesday. On Tuesday, October's NFIB Business Optimism Index is scheduled for release. Initial jobless claims numbers are due on Thursday.

Philadelphia Fed President Patrick Harker speaks on "Federal Reserve Balance-Sheet Normalization" before the 'Global Interdependence Center Central Banking Series: Japan' in Tokyo on Sunday. St. Louis Fed chief James Bullard gives a presentation on the U.S. economy and monetary policy before the 'Economic Update Breakfast' hosted by the Association for Corporate Growth and the Federal Reserve Bank of St. Louis Louisville branch on Tuesday. On the same day, Atlanta Fed President Raphael Bostic speaks on the economic outlook and monetary policy before the 35th Annual Business and Economic Forum hosted by Auburn University Montgomery, the Montgomery Chamber of Commerce and the Montgomery Area Committee of 100. Chicago Fed chief Charles Evans speaks on the economy in a panel before the UBS European Conference in London on Wednesday, while Boston Fed President Eric Rosengren speaks on the economy before the Northeastern University Economic Policy Forum in Boston. Also on Wednesday, New York Fed releases the text of a speech by Executive Vice President (Legal Group) Michael Held, on "The Financial Crisis: Perspectives from a Decade On," delivered before a closed joint meeting of the Administrative and Banking Law Committee organized by the New York City Bar Association. On Thursday, Cleveland Fed chief Loretta Mester speaks before the Cato Institute 35th Annual Monetary Conference in Washington. Fed President Robert Kaplan participates in a moderated Q&A session before the CFA Society Houston on the same day. Fed Board Governor Lael Brainard speaks on "Fintech" before the Third Annual Financial Stability Conference hosted by the U.S. Treasury Dept. Office of Financial Research and the University of Michigan Center on Finance, Law, and Policy in Ann Arbor, also on Thursday.

The world's largest networking-gear maker Cisco Systems Inc reports first-quarter results on Wednesday and earnings are likely to have been hurt by continuing declines in its traditional business of making switches and routers. Analysts and investors will be on the lookout for company's diversification strategy after its $1.71-billion acquisition of BroadSoft Inc in October.

The No. 1 U.S. home improvement chain Home Depot Inc reports third-quarter earnings on Tuesday that are likely to have benefited from demand for home essentials and restoration equipment during and in the aftermath of powerful hurricanes in the quarter.

On Thursday, chip gear maker Applied Materials Inc reports fourth-quarter earnings, which are likely to have benefited from strong demand from smartphone makers, coupled with strength in its display business.

TJX Cos Inc, the operator of TJMaxx discount stores, reports third-quarter earnings on Tuesday. The results are expected to reflect a growth in sales as the company's off-price model attracted bargain-hungry shoppers. Investors will look forward to comments on the impact of the hurricanes in early October on the company's holiday-quarter and full-year forecasts.

Target Corp reports third-quarter earnings on Wednesday and the results are likely to show the retailer enjoyed sales growth due to the launch of private label brands to cater to changing tastes of consumers ahead of the holiday season. Investors will be looking forward to comments on margin pressure in the fourth quarter, a period of fierce price competition.

Viacom Inc, the owner of MTV, Comedy Central and the Paramount film studio, reports fourth-quarter earnings on Thursday. Its domestic affiliate revenue, the fees it collects from cable TV operators as well as online distributors, is expected to dip. In October, Viacom and Charter Communications agreed to a distribution deal that puts eight of Viacom's most popular networks in Charter's cheapest U.S. cable bundle, a source told Reuters.

When Best Buy Co Inc reports third-quarter results on Thursday, all eyes will be on the electronics retailer's fourth-quarter forecast, with the holiday months historically making up nearly half of the company's profit.

Folgers coffee maker J M Smucker Co, which reports second-quarter earnings on Thursday, trimmed its full-year earnings forecast in August, citing weak demand for coffee as retailers placed fewer orders due to the rising cost of coffee. The company lowered prices in response, which hit margins, but said it expects better margins further into the year.

Clothing retailer Gap Inc reports third-quarter results on Thursday. The company's earnings are expected to have benefited from a boost in demand for its lower-end Old Navy apparel and activewear brand Athleta.

Teen apparel retailer Abercrombie & Fitch Co is expected to post stronger third-quarter sales growth on Friday as the company's initiatives to boost demand for its Hollister brand is paying off. However, demand for its namesake and other brands remain stagnant, unable to replicate the success of its surfwear brand.

Chinese financial planning platform Jianpu Technology Inc, a unit of fintech firm Rong360, intends to debut its ADS on the New York Stock Exchange under the symbol "JT" on Thursday. The 22.5-million ADS offering is expected to raise about $213.8 million at the mid-point of the proposed range of $8.50 and $10.50 per ADS.

The biggest and most high-profile U.S. money managers and hedge fund investors, including George Soros, David Tepper, David Einhorn and Carl Icahn, will issue regulatory filings on Monday and Tuesday that shows the change in their holding in stocks and assets classes. The filings will reveal market trends, including whether bearish billionaire investors threw in the towel and bought U.S. stocks at the start of the second half of the year.

General Motors Co Chief Executive Mary Barra will speak to investors at the Barclays 2017 Global Automotive Conference on Wednesday. Investors have been encouraged by Barra's efforts to convince Wall Street that GM can deliver strong profits, even if U.S. sales slow, and her moves to restructure the company and invest in electric and autonomous cars. However, GM's earnings have lagged the S&P 500 average.

The main economic data release in Canada next week will be the consumer price index, due on Friday. It is expected to show the annual inflation rate cooled to 1.4 percent in October, which will likely give the Bank of Canada room to take its time raising interest rates after two back-to-back hikes earlier this year. Manufacturing sales, due on Thursday, are forecast to have declined by 0.2 percent in September, in line with slower economic growth in the second half of the year, after a strong first six months. On Wednesday, Bank of Canada Senior Deputy Governor Carolyn Wilkins will give a speech in New York on monetary policy under uncertainty. Markets will watch her comments for signs of how the central bank will navigate the number of unknowns Canada is facing, including soft inflation and the renegotiation of the North American Free Trade Agreement.

ON MONDAY

The Federal budget numbers for October kicks off a busy week on the economic calendar. The Congressional Budget Office is likely to show a deficit of $50 billion. (1400/1900)

Tyson Foods Inc, the No. 1 U.S. meat processor, reports fourth-quarter earnings, which likely benefited from higher sales due to surging demand for chicken in the United States. However falling poultry and beef prices may have been a slight dampener.

LIVECHAT – REUTERS INVESTMENT SUMMIT Richard Bernstein of Richard Bernstein Advisors, a much-noted expert on equity, style and asset allocation, will deliver a top-down take on the 2018 investment landscape. (1530/2030) To join the Global Markets Forum, click here http://tmsnrt.rs/2lExMPr

RPT-Small banks oppose U.S. regulator offering olive branch to tech sector - Reuters News

{{20171109T120002.058+0000}}RPT-Small banks oppose U.S. regulator offering olive branch to tech sector(Repeats story published Wednesday)

By Dan Freed and Pete Schroeder

NEW YORK/WASHINGTON, Nov 9 (Reuters) - Small Main Street banks vowed on Wednesday to fight any review of a ban that prevents retailers such as Wal-Mart Stores Inc and tech companies like Amazon.com Inc from becoming fully fledged banks.

Keith Noreika, a top U.S. banking regulator, stirred disquiet among community bankers with his call for a review of the current regulations. The proposal by the acting Comptroller of the Currency (OCC) was made at a banking conference in New York and comes as technology companies such as Amazon and Apple Inc have already broken into the financial arena with payment services and different types of lending. [nL1N1NE0UY]

"Mixing banking and commerce is a bad idea that keeps recurring like a bad dream," said Paul Merski with the Independent Community Bankers of America.

"It's one of our bedrock resolutions to oppose the threat of full blown mixing of banking and commerce."

Mixing banking and other commercial activities has traditionally been prohibited in the United States, amid fears customer deposits would be used to fund or subsidize unrelated and potentially risky non-banking business.

Even so, technology companies have been making inroads.

Earlier this week, Apple released a product called Apple Pay Cash. The feature allows iPhone users to send each other cash that can then immediately be used in stores that take Apple Pay. The system uses a so-called "virtual debit card" to enable in-store payments. Amazon, meanwhile, offers small-business lending.

Nonetheless, Wells Fargo & Co Chief Executive Tim Sloan said he does not view Silicon Valley as a threat to banks. "I don't think Apple fundamentally wants to become a bank. I don't think Amazon wants to become a bank," he said during a CEO round table at an industry conference in New York Tuesday. "They want to use financial services products to help their customers succeed."

Amazon had no immediate comment and Apple did not return a request for comment.

THE NEXT FDIC BOSS

Technology firms would have to submit to a welter of regulation and oversight and apply for a banking charter from the OCC if they wanted to become full-service banks. Bank holding companies are also prohibited from engaging in nonfinancial activities.

In a statement, Colin Walsh the CEO of mobile banking startup Varo Money, said its charter application was going through the approval process. Student online lender Social Finance Inc withdrew its application last month. [nL2N1LU21P] [nL2N1MO1LK]

Mobile payments company Square , which reported better-than-expected results on Wednesday, has applied to be a so-called industrial loan company, an entity that enjoys some of the same privileges as a traditional bank but falls short of a full bank charter. [nL3N1NE6DM]

"It (industrial loan charter) does allow us to engage more directly with regulatory bodies so it's great to hear that comment coming today from the OCC," said Sarah Friar, the chief financial officer of Square.

The comments from Noreika, who has built up a reputation for a strong deregulatory bent since taking over in May, puts a spotlight on the OCC's sister organization the Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation (FDIC).

While the OCC issues the bank charter, the FDIC insures any deposits and must also approve the charter.

The term of current FDIC Chairman Martin Gruenberg, a holdover from the administration of former President Barack Obama, expires this month. Gruenberg has the option of staying on as chairman until his replacement is nominated and confirmed by the Senate.

Some bankers said they were comfortable with corporations entering their turf, as long as they were subject to the same rules.

"If Wal-Mart wants to be a bank that's fine, as long as they make the appropriate investments to protect the parts of the banking system that are so critical," said Kelly King, chief executive at regional lender BB&T Corp .

King added that he was "absolutely opposed" to the idea of a limited banking license.

Wal-Mart, the world's largest retailer, abandoned plans for its own bank in 2007 after opposition from lawmakers, bankers and watchdog groups.

Wal-Mart does not intend to resurrect those plans after Noreika's comments, spokeswoman Erin Hulliberger said.

Wal-Mart already operates hundreds of money centers within its stores, which offer services like check cashing, money transfers, bill payment along with prepaid debit cards and credit cards.

Facebook Inc in 2015 began letting people send money to friends through its Messenger app, but a move into banking is not on the company's roadmap, said spokeswoman Vanessa Chan.

Wal-Mart gears up to compete on Black Friday - Reuters News

{{20171109T050100.701+0000}}Wal-Mart gears up to compete on Black FridayNov 9 (Reuters) - Wal-Mart Stores Inc said on Thursday its U.S. stores will feature color-coded sections for different product categories on Black Friday, as it prepares to compete for shoppers on one of the busiest shopping days of the year.

Toys, electronics, apparel and other departments will be color-coded in store for the first time so that shoppers can easily find deals. The codes will be available on the retailer's Black Friday circular and store maps.

For years, Black Friday has marked the start of the holiday shopping season in the United States with retailers offering steep discounts. But its popularity has been on the wane with the rise of online shopping and inexpensive deals throughout the year.

The holiday shopping season, which runs through Christmas on Dec. 25, can account for as much as 40 percent of retailers' annual sales.

Steve Bratspies, Wal-Mart's chief merchandising officer, told reporters on a conference call that the retailer is prepared to draw in shoppers this holiday season.

"We know the categories and items customers are looking for, have focused our assortment on those top items, pricing them so we cannot be beat and buying deep to ensure more availability," he said.

Wal-Mart will kick off Black Friday deals at 12:01 a.m. EST online on Thanksgiving morning and at 6 p.m. local time in its stores.

(Reporting by Nandita Bose in Chicago; Editing by Matthew Lewis) ((nandita.bose@thomsonreuters.com)(+ 1 312 408-8726)(Reuters Messaging: nandita.bose.reuters.com@reuters.net))
